('86', 1, 6, 7, 1666) 4. LETTER TO GOPALASWAMI AYYANGAR
('86', 1, 7, 8, 1700) SEVAGRAM, March 5, 1945
('86', 1, 8, 9, 1724) DEAR FRIEND, I was delighted to hear from you.
('86', 1, 8, 10, 1771) I entirely agree with you regarding the States.
('86', 1, 8, 11, 1819) As to foreign rule, I could not open the subject with Q.A. Jinnah.
('86', 1, 8, 12, 1886) He has excluded the States from his calculation.
('86', 1, 8, 13, 1935) You have not expected me to give any thought to the rest of your scheme.
('86', 1, 8, 14, 2008) For my opinion is that when the whole of foreign rule goes from the whole of India, then only we shall be free to think with a true sense of responsibility.
('86', 1, 9, 15, 2165) Yours sincerely, M. K. GANDHI SJT.

('86', 4, 6, 15, 5461) 11. NOTE TO GOPE GURBUXANI
('86', 4, 7, 16, 5488) March 5, 1945 Brahmacharya plays an important role in subduing the brute within us.
('86', 4, 7, 17, 5572) This is my definition: Brahmacharya is that path by which we realize the Brahman.
('86', 4, 7, 18, 5654) This path lies in completely controlling the five sense organs, the five moter organs and the eleventh, the mind.
('86', 4, 7, 19, 5768) I have deliberately replied in Hindustani.
('86', 4, 8, 20, 5811) From the Hindi original: G.N. 1322
('86', 4, 9, 21, 5846) 1 A Congress Worker of U. P. 2 The addressee had asked: What part does brahmacharya play in the subjugation of the flesh and what is your definition of the word brahmacharya for married people?

('86', 5, 1, 2, 6080) 12. INTERVIEW TO ORIENT PRESS
('86', 5, 2, 3, 6110) March 5, 1945 1
('86', 5, 3, 4, 6126) When asked by the representative of the Orient Press on what he had to say about the recent warning given to local Congress workers by the District Magistrate, Nagpur, 2 Gandhiji said: Congressmen who have associated for the fulfilment of our constructive programme need not be agitated over what local governments say or do.
('86', 5, 3, 5, 6452) Whether their policy is merely local or represents the Centre, they should learn to shed fear.
('86', 5, 3, 6, 6547) The District Magistrates strictures if they are properly reported are undoubtedly revealing.
('86', 5, 3, 7, 6640) They need not alarm us.
('86', 5, 4, 8, 6664) In reply to another question as to how without any political action and only by social and economic improvement the country could reach its destined goal as revealed by him in his statement published on 20th February, 3 Gandhiji replied: I must refer you to my statement and you may ask yourself whether, if the programme is universally responded to, it will not lead to swaraj.
('86', 5, 4, 9, 7043) Indeed the Muslim League and even the Government should join in its prosecution if they are honest about independence.
('86', 5, 5, 10, 7162) When asked what he thought about anti Indian propaganda carried on in America by Britishers Gandhiji replied: Anti Indian British propaganda should not matter if we are truthful.
('86', 5, 5, 11, 7341) The Hitavada, 6 3 1945
('86', 5, 6, 12, 7364) 1 The Hindu, 6 3 1945, however, reports this under the date March 4, 1945. 2 The Additional District Magistrate, Nagpur, had told Congressmen that activities banned in the name of the Congress could not be carried on in the name of any camouflaged Congress organization.
('86', 5, 6, 13, 7635) He had mentioned such organizations as the Nagpur Provincial Congress Representative Committees,the Political Prisoners Aid Committee and Congress Ward Committees and warned that action could be taken against them under the Restrictions and Detention Ordinance.
('86', 5, 6, 14, 7897) 3 Vide Statement to the Press, 17 2 1945.
('86', 6, 0, 1, 7939) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 7

('86', 7, 1, 2, 8996) 16. LETTER TO MUNNALAL G. SHAH
('86', 7, 2, 3, 9027) March 6, 1945
('86', 7, 3, 4, 9041) MU., Why need you feel embarrassed?
('86', 7, 3, 5, 9077) This problem cannot be solved in that way.
('86', 7, 3, 6, 9120) Ask me any question you wish without the slightest hesitation.
('86', 7, 3, 7, 9183) My statement has undergone some revision and may undergo more.
('86', 7, 3, 8, 9246) I dont wish to exclude anybody.
('86', 7, 3, 9, 9278) I have mentioned four.
('86', 7, 3, 10, 9301) Perhaps they will say, We were not objects of your experiment; we slept with you as with a mother. I would not contradict them.
('86', 7, 3, 11, 9429) It is enough here to mention that such a thing has happened.
('86', 7, 3, 12, 9490) I dont consider Abha, Kanchan and Vina as part of the experiment.
('86', 7, 3, 13, 9556) If we distinguish between sleeping together and the experiment, the difference between the two in my view is a big one.
('86', 7, 3, 14, 9676) Abha slept with me for hardly three nights.
('86', 7, 3, 15, 9720) Kanchan slept one night only.
('86', 7, 3, 16, 9750) Vinas sleeping with me might be called an accident.
('86', 7, 3, 17, 9802) All that can be said is that she slept close to me.
('86', 7, 3, 18, 9854) If Abha had continued, her case would have been and altogether different one.
('86', 7, 3, 19, 9932) Kanchans case was rather tragic.
('86', 7, 3, 20, 9965) I didnt understand her at all.
('86', 7, 3, 21, 9996) What Abha or Kanchan told me was this; that she had no intention whatever of observing brahmacharya, butwished to enjoy the pleasure of sex.
('86', 7, 3, 22, 10137) She, therefore, stayed only reluctantly and undressed only for fear of hurting me.
('86', 7, 3, 23, 10220) If I remember rightly, she was not with me even for an hour.
('86', 7, 3, 24, 10281) I then stopped both the women sleeping with me, for I realized that Kanu and you were upset.
('86', 7, 3, 25, 10374) I myself advised them that they should tell you both and also Bhansali.
('86', 7, 3, 26, 10446) You will thus see that these three names cannot be included in the experiment.
('86', 7, 3, 27, 10525) Lilavati, Amtussalaam, Rajkumari and Prabhavati are not here.
('86', 7, 3, 28, 10587) I have deliberately included Pra.
('86', 7, 3, 29, 10621) in the experiment.
('86', 7, 3, 30, 10640) Maybe I should not.
('86', 7, 3, 31, 10660) She often used to sleep with me to keep me warm even before I was conscious that I was making an experiment.
('86', 7, 3, 32, 10769) I used to draw her to me when she lay on the floor, shivering, for my sake.
('86', 7, 3, 33, 10845) This is an old, old story.
('86', 7, 3, 34, 10872) I think I have now told you everything.
('86', 7, 3, 35, 10912) If you have any more questions, you may ask me.
('86', 7, 3, 36, 10960) Kanchans labouring under a misunderstanding pained me, but I was helpless.
('86', 7, 3, 37, 11035) I formed no judgment regarding Sushila and you.
('86', 7, 3, 38, 11083) I did not get sufficient material, for doing that either.
('86', 7, 3, 39, 11141) If she herself wishes and you too wish it, I would spare some time and hear you both.
('86', 7, 3, 40, 11227) I will examine witnesses and try to weigh the evidence.
('86', 7, 3, 41, 11283) But let me repeat that if you
('86', 8, 0, 1, 11313) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 9
('86', 8, 1, 2, 11352) two feel as brother and sister to each other, you should not ask even your father to examine you and pronounce judgment.
('86', 8, 1, 3, 11473) But do as you wish.
('86', 8, 1, 4, 11493) I understand about a separate kitchen.
('86', 8, 1, 5, 11532) I shall try.
('86', 8, 1, 6, 11545) Will the purchase of provisions for the hospital and the Ashram kitchens be under one account or two?
('86', 8, 1, 7, 11647) I see that a catering service can be run only if it is managed by a third party.
('86', 8, 1, 8, 11728) I think this is enough for today.
('86', 8, 1, 9, 11762) About the third party and going to villages, etc., later on.
('86', 8, 1, 10, 11823) I have not revised this.
('86', 8, 1, 11, 11848) If you feel that anything needs correction, ask me.

('86', 9, 5, 9, 13002) 19. NOTE TO MUNNALAL G. SHAH 1
('86', 9, 6, 10, 13033) March 6, 1945 This discussion is somewhat out of place because at present nothing is happening.
('86', 9, 6, 11, 13129) For this too friends are responsible.
('86', 9, 6, 12, 13167) I have gone as far as I could to satisfy them.
('86', 9, 6, 13, 13214) It will not be proper for me to do anything until I have satisfied my co workers.
('86', 9, 6, 14, 13296) I am as much against compromise as I am for it.
('86', 9, 6, 15, 13344) For this very reason my elder brother remained my enemy for 13 years.
('86', 9, 6, 16, 13414) He asked my forgiveness five or six months before his death.
('86', 9, 6, 17, 13475) My caste also became my enemy in the same manner.
('86', 9, 6, 18, 13525) Now it does not show any feeling of animosity.
('86', 9, 6, 19, 13572) But quite a few sanatanists are still opposed to me.
('86', 9, 6, 20, 13625) On this account I let myself be deprived of lakhs of rupees.
('86', 9, 6, 21, 13686) I used to be a friend of the Empire.
('86', 9, 6, 22, 13723) Today I have become its enemy.
('86', 9, 6, 23, 13754) What more need I say?
('86', 9, 6, 24, 13776) I showed the door to a wife like Ba.
('86', 9, 6, 25, 13813) Thus, I am what I am.
('86', 9, 6, 26, 13835) There is therefore no point in talking about the welfare of society.
('86', 9, 6, 27, 13904) What else may I give up?
('86', 9, 6, 28, 13929) I cannot give up thinking.
('86', 9, 6, 29, 13956) As far as possible I have postponed the practice of sleeping together.
('86', 9, 6, 30, 14027) But it cannot be given up altogether.
('86', 9, 6, 31, 14065) You can say that ever since I went to England I have been pursuing the idea of brahmacharya.
('86', 9, 6, 32, 14158) It has not harmed anyone.
('86', 9, 6, 33, 14184) It is true of course that I should do what others too can be permitted to do.
('86', 9, 6, 34, 14262) If I can restrain myself and sleep beside a woman, others can also do so on the same condition.
('86', 9, 6, 35, 14358) They can fulfil that condition if they so wish.
('86', 9, 6, 36, 14406) The same applies to non violence.
('86', 9, 6, 37, 14440) If I completely give up sleeping together, my brahmacharya will be put to shame.
('86', 9, 6, 38, 14521) It is not that I would do anything for the mere pleasure of it.
('86', 9, 6, 39, 14585) I have not done it
('86', 9, 7, 40, 14604) 1 Gandhiji wrote this for the addressee when the latter met him at 3.30 p.
('86', 10, 0, 1, 14679) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 11
('86', 10, 1, 2, 14719) for years, and I shall not do it now.
('86', 10, 1, 3, 14757) It is true that people may indulge in licentiousness by imitating me.
('86', 10, 1, 4, 14827) Who can stop it?
('86', 10, 1, 5, 14844) Is there any place where asatyagraha 1 has never been practised in the name of satyagraha?
('86', 10, 1, 6, 14935) In any case, the thing has been postponed because it calls for consideration.
('86', 10, 1, 7, 15013) But since there is need for a halt let it be so.
('86', 10, 1, 8, 15062) You can ask any questions.
('86', 10, 1, 9, 15089) I suggest that you should not ask questions individually.You may all discuss it among yourselves and then ask questions.
('86', 10, 1, 10, 15210) Let it be understood that right now everything is postponed.
('86', 10, 1, 11, 15271) Manu has been left alone by the others.
('86', 10, 1, 12, 15311) Hence there is scope for a mature deliberation.
('86', 10, 1, 13, 15359) I claim that whatever I have done I have done in the name of God.
('86', 10, 1, 14, 15425) I go to bed reciting His name.
('86', 10, 1, 15, 15456) I have got up with His name on my lips.
('86', 10, 1, 16, 15496) So it is in my dreams, whether alone or with some woman.
('86', 10, 1, 17, 15553) What God will make me do in days to come He alone knows.
('86', 10, 1, 18, 15610) Such restrictions should not be imosed on me.
('86', 10, 1, 19, 15656) Kishorelalbhais business should be left to him.
('86', 10, 1, 20, 15704) Do not drag him into this matter.
('86', 10, 1, 21, 15738) My advice is that everybody should join hands and stand by him.
('86', 10, 1, 22, 15802) There is no need to plead his case before me.
('86', 10, 1, 23, 15848) I am glad that I have answered your question but I am not in a position to listen.
('86', 10, 1, 24, 15931) I have said that right now everything stands postponed, leaving aside Manu.
('86', 10, 1, 25, 16007) But Kishorelal is not satisfied with this.
('86', 10, 1, 26, 16050) It is your duty to understand him.
('86', 10, 1, 27, 16085) He is right when he says: I was not consulted at first.
('86', 10, 1, 28, 16141) Now I shall not create any confusion. In the present situation whoever has any doubt in his mind should follow him.
('86', 10, 1, 29, 16257) I would in any case do that.
('86', 10, 1, 30, 16286) I would not create difficulties for him.
('86', 10, 1, 31, 16327) You should consider his delicate health when you bother him.
('86', 10, 1, 32, 16388) If you do this you will be serving him, no doubt, but you will also be serving me.
('86', 10, 1, 33, 16471) My love for him is certainly no less than my love for my brother.
('86', 10, 1, 34, 16537) What more can I do?
('86', 10, 2, 35, 16557) From a copy of the Hindi: C.W. 5891. Courtesy: Munnalal G. Shah
('86', 10, 3, 36, 16621) 20. FOREWORD TO GANDHIJIS CORRESPONDENCE WITH THE GOVERNMENT
('86', 10, 4, 37, 16682) I have read the introduction as also the originals.
('86', 10, 4, 38, 16734) The introduction may be good enough for the hasty reader, but the publication is not designed for the hasty reader.
('86', 10, 4, 39, 16850) It is designed for the
('86', 10, 5, 40, 16873) 1 Opposite of satyagraha.
('86', 11, 0, 1, 16899) 12 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('86', 11, 1, 2, 16940) serious worker who can affect the politics of his country and even the world affairs.
('86', 11, 1, 3, 17026) To such my advice is that he must read the originals.
('86', 11, 1, 4, 17080) The introduction may be used as such and as an aid to memory.
('86', 11, 1, 5, 17142) I want the readers I have in view to take me at my word.
('86', 11, 1, 6, 17199) I have written as I felt at the moment as a seeker of long standing of Truth and Non violence.
('86', 11, 1, 7, 17294) I have written without reservation and without embellishment.
('86', 11, 1, 8, 17356) After my accidentally premature discharge from detention 1 and convalescence I studied from reliable witnesses the happenings of the two years after the incarceration of principal Congressmen and myself.
('86', 11, 1, 9, 17560) I have heard nothing to modify the opinion expressed in my writings under review.
('86', 11, 1, 10, 17642) I know first hand what has happened, since my discharge, in the various spheres of life.
('86', 11, 1, 11, 17731) And I have found bitter confirmation of what I have said in the following pages.
('86', 11, 1, 12, 17812) Indeed, the whole of India is a vast prison.
('86', 11, 1, 13, 17857) The Viceroy is the irresponsible superintendent of the prison with numerous jailers and warders under him.
('86', 11, 1, 14, 17964) The four hundred millions of India are not the only prisoners.
('86', 11, 1, 15, 18027) There are others similarly situated in the other parts of the earth under other superintendents.
('86', 11, 1, 16, 18124) A jailer is as much a prisoner as his prisoner.
('86', 11, 1, 17, 18172) There is no doubt a difference.
('86', 11, 1, 18, 18204) From my point of view he is worse.
('86', 11, 1, 19, 18239) If there is a Day of Judgment, i.e., if there is a Judge whom we do not see but who nevertheless is much more truly than we exist for a brief moment, the judgment will go hard against the Jailer and in favour of the prisoners.
('86', 11, 1, 20, 18466) India is the only place on earth which knowingly has chosen Truth and Non violence as the only means for her deliverance.
('86', 11, 1, 21, 18588) But deliverance to be obtained through these means must be deliverance for the whole world including the jailers otherwise described by me as tyrants and imperialists.
('86', 11, 1, 22, 18756) I need not mention Fascists or Nazis or Japanese.
('86', 11, 1, 23, 18806) They seem to be as good as gone.
('86', 11, 1, 24, 18839) The war will end this year or the next.
('86', 11, 1, 25, 18879) It will bring victory to the Allies.
('86', 11, 1, 26, 18916) The pity of it is that it will be only so called if it is attained with India and the like lying prostrate at the feet of the Allies.
('86', 11, 1, 27, 19050) That victory will be assuredly a prelude to a deadlier war, if anything could be more deadly.
('86', 11, 1, 28, 19144) I know that I do not need to plead for non violent India.
('86', 11, 1, 29, 19202) If India has the coin with Truth on one face and Non violence on the
('86', 11, 2, 30, 19271) 1 On May 6, 1944
('86', 12, 0, 1, 19288) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 13
('86', 12, 1, 2, 19328) other, the coin has its own inestimable value which will speak for itself.
('86', 12, 1, 3, 19403) Truth and Non violence must express humility at every step.
('86', 12, 1, 4, 19463) They do not disdain real aid from any quarter, much less from those in whose name and for whom exploitation is practised.
('86', 12, 1, 5, 19585) If the British and the Allies aid, so much the better.
('86', 12, 1, 6, 19640) Deliverance will then come sooner.
('86', 12, 1, 7, 19675) If they do not, deliverance is still certain.
('86', 12, 1, 8, 19721) Only the agony of the victim will be greater, the time longer.
('86', 12, 1, 9, 19784) But what are agony and time if theyare spent in favour of liberty, especially when it is to be brought about through Truth and Non violence!
('86', 12, 2, 10, 19925) M. K. GANDHI SEVAGRAM, March 7, 1945

('86', 12, 4, 13, 20030) 21. FOREWORD TO AHAR ANE POSHAN
('86', 12, 5, 14, 20062) Bhai Jhaverbhai has ever been undertaking new studies and adding to his store of useful knowledge.
('86', 12, 5, 15, 20161) He easily finds use for this increased knowledge in disseminating it.
('86', 12, 5, 16, 20231) He thinks in his own language or the national language, so that his ideas are understood by thousands with the utmost ease.
('86', 12, 5, 17, 20355) If he carries on in this manner, the knowledge he has gained will soon become common possession.
('86', 12, 5, 18, 20452) Bhai Jhaverbhai has written a beautiful essay and given information about food, etc., in simple language.
('86', 12, 5, 19, 20558) I hope that the knowledge will be widely used and the suggestions made in the essay implemented.
('86', 12, 5, 20, 20655) The authors aim is to impart knowledge so that it will be put to use and not merely add to learning.

('86', 17, 1, 2, 25796) 31. LETTER TO KRISHNACHANDRA
('86', 17, 2, 3, 25825) March 7, 1945
('86', 17, 3, 4, 25839) KRISHNACHANDRA, There is no discourtesy in your question.
('86', 17, 3, 5, 25897) Your question shows how imperfect a medium language is.
('86', 17, 3, 6, 25953) If I stop sleeping together for all time it will mean that I have been mistaken.
('86', 17, 3, 7, 26034) Otherwise why should I stop it?
('86', 17, 3, 8, 26066) There is a limit toabstaining from it for the sake of friends.
('86', 17, 3, 9, 26129) Sleeping together came with my taking up of brahmacharya or even before that.
('86', 17, 3, 10, 26207) Can you understand it now?
('86', 17, 3, 11, 26234) The dangers you have pointed out are certainly there.
('86', 17, 3, 12, 26288) But for that reason, a good act should not be avoided.
('86', 17, 3, 13, 26343) Only we should be vigilant.
('86', 17, 3, 14, 26371) The experiment is not meant to be imitated.
('86', 17, 3, 15, 26415) But if I can become a perfect brahmachari thereby, would I not be able to contribute more to the welfare of the world?
('86', 17, 3, 16, 26534) Even if there is a single person who can train himself that way, he should do it.
('86', 17, 3, 17, 26616) I was not out for an experiment, but when the situation presented itself before me I did what I felt was necessary.

('86', 25, 1, 2, 34720) 48. INTERVIEW TO ANDHRA DEPUTATION 1
('86', 25, 2, 3, 34757) SEVAGRAM, March 9, 1945 2
('86', 25, 3, 4, 34783) (1) Q. At present there are only provincial Congress organizations functioning.
('86', 25, 3, 5, 34863) Is it not essential to have an all India Congress organization to enunciate a common policy and common programme?
('86', 25, 4, 6, 34977) A. A common all India Congress organization is an impossibility while the President and other members of the Working Committee are in detention.
('86', 25, 5, 7, 35122) (2) Q. What is the definition of a kisan?
('86', 25, 5, 8, 35164) We hope that you agree that we can have an independent Andhra Provincial Kisan Congress as a part of and under the discipline of the Andhra Province Congress Assembly [sic]?
('86', 25, 6, 9, 35338) A. For me a kisan is one who actually works on land belonging to himself or another.
('86', 25, 6, 10, 35423) In every case, I have pointed the way of relief.
('86', 25, 6, 11, 35472) You should read what I have written.
('86', 25, 6, 12, 35509) 3 Local difficulties should be solved locally.
('86', 25, 6, 13, 35556) For the right answer, accurate knowledge of local conditions is necessary.
('86', 25, 6, 14, 35631) I lack this.
('86', 25, 6, 15, 35644) Hence my answer may even mislead.
('86', 25, 6, 16, 35678) All organizations may be independent and yet a part of the Congress and subject to its discipline.
('86', 25, 7, 17, 35777) (3) Q. We think it is better to have for the Kisan Congress also a tricoloured national flag without any additional class emblem.
('86', 25, 8, 18, 35907) A. I had full discussion with Prof.
('86', 25, 8, 19, 35943) 4 I agree generally about the points you have raised.
('86', 25, 9, 20, 35997) (4) Q. There are many kisans in villages who have helped in war efforts under the official influence.
('86', 25, 9, 21, 36099) They are not entitled to be members of the Congress organizations at present.
('86', 25, 9, 22, 36177) But they are, all the same, sympathizers of the National Congress.
('86', 25, 9, 23, 36244) Shall we bring them into Kisan Congress?
('86', 25, 9, 24, 36285) Both classes of members can have equal voice in the matter of redress against the landlords and the Government.
('86', 25, 9, 25, 36397) But the first class of members only should decide all questions of a political nature.
('86', 25, 10, 26, 36484) A. Those who are real sympathizers will remain so even if for
('86', 25, 11, 27, 36546) 1 The deputation consisted of Congress workers from Andhra, including Chandramouli, Kaleshwar Rao, Prof.
('86', 25, 11, 28, 36651) Ranga and others.
('86', 25, 11, 29, 36669) 2 Prow The Bombay Chronicle, 10 3 1945 3 Vide Hints for Constructive Workers, 22 10 1944. 4 Vide Interview to N. G. Ranga, 29 10 1944 and Interview to N. G. Ranga, 28 11 1944.
('86', 26, 0, 1, 36845) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 27
('86', 26, 1, 2, 36885) technical reasons today they may not join you.
('86', 26, 1, 3, 36932) By all means take them if you so wish.
('86', 26, 2, 4, 36971) The Deputation asked Gandhiji whether Congress could see local officials in grave and emergent cases of food and other economic difficulties of people for immediate redress and Gandhiji replied that it was not an absolute evil to see officials but there should be no seeing to flatter or please them.
('86', 26, 3, 5, 37272) Asked as to whether Congress bodies could apply to officials for permission to hold public meetings, processions or training camps, in any district where prohibitory order by the District Magistrate is in force, Gandhiji replied that no such permission should be applied for.
('86', 26, 4, 6, 37548) Winding up the discussion, Mahatmaji said that generally while he made himself available to all friends, they should try to act on their own even though they may make mistakes.

('86', 32, 12, 20, 43427) 64. STATEMENT TO THE PRESS
('86', 32, 13, 21, 43454) SEVAGRAM, March 11, 1945 A conference of Congress workers, limited in number and by special invitation, was recently banned in Akola by the District Magistrate.
('86', 32, 13, 22, 43615) The order is reported to say that discussion will take
('86', 32, 14, 23, 43670) 1 Raja Narendranath, addressees father, died on March 10.
('86', 33, 0, 1, 43728) 34 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('86', 33, 1, 2, 43769) place among other subjects on the work and programme of the Congress, particularly in villages.
('86', 33, 1, 3, 43865) Considering the influence of the invitees, he was of the opinion that this conference would hamper the successful prosecution of the war.
('86', 33, 1, 4, 44003) It passes comprehension how a conference, where only discussion could take place, can hamper the prosecution of the war or how the constructive programme, no matter how influentially worked, can hamper the prosecution of the war.
('86', 33, 1, 5, 44233) Does the Magistrate say one thing and mean something else when he says that a successful working of the constructive programme can and will make the present war with the Japanese impossible?
('86', 33, 1, 6, 44424) This may need proof, but no proof is needed to show that the constructive work cannot and is not designed to hamper in any way whatsoever the prosecution of the war.
('86', 33, 1, 7, 44590) What it can do is to bring work and bread to villagers in their own homes, besides making illiterates literate and happy.
('86', 33, 1, 8, 44712) Or does Government, if the order is prompted by them, want to prevent influential Congressmen from serving the people in any way whatsoever?
('86', 33, 1, 9, 44853) If so, why have they released Congressmen at all?
('86', 33, 1, 10, 44903) Anyway Congressmen whose only calling is service of the people will serve mutely and without caring for the consequences that may befall them by reason of their service.
('86', 33, 1, 11, 45073) That is the true meaning of do or die.
('86', 33, 1, 12, 45112) The Hindu, 13 3 1945
('86', 33, 2, 13, 45133) 65. LETTER TO KANAM GANDHI March 11, 1945

('86', 37, 1, 2, 49388) 72. LETTER TO MUNNALAL G. SHAH March 12, 1945
('86', 37, 2, 3, 49434) MUNNALAL, I can find the time, but it seems pointless.
('86', 37, 2, 4, 49489) Since you want it I give my decision.
('86', 37, 2, 5, 49527) Both of you are hasty.
('86', 37, 2, 6, 49550) Both of you first say whatever occurs to you and think afterwards.
('86', 37, 2, 7, 49617) If Sushila had not intervened that evening, the outcome would have been quite different.
('86', 37, 2, 8, 49706) But she is unable to restrain herself.
('86', 37, 2, 9, 49745) Moreover, she believes she cannot hurt you since you are more than a brother to her.
('86', 37, 2, 10, 49830) There is nothing more left for me to say.
('86', 37, 2, 11, 49872) What has happened has happened.
('86', 37, 2, 12, 49904) Sushila could not have removed Chand to quarters reserved for other people, and she assumed that since she had come with a suggestion about the sick, you would readily offer your room.
('86', 37, 2, 13, 50089) The thing is we ought to have special facilities for the sick, which we have not provided.
('86', 37, 2, 14, 50180) It will be enough if we take a lesson for the future from this incident.
('86', 37, 2, 15, 50253) Say to yourself again and again: Think before you speak. As far as possible one must cultivate silence.
('86', 37, 2, 16, 50357) And even if we have to work very hard for it, we must have a separate room for the sick.
('86', 37, 2, 17, 50446) Like a fire bucket, it must not be put to any other use.
('86', 37, 2, 18, 50503) Sushilas statement is attached, as also yours.
('86', 37, 2, 19, 50550) I have not shown her this letter, nor your statement.
('86', 37, 2, 20, 50604) BAPU From a photostat of the Gujarati: C.W. 5849. Courtesy: Munnalal G. Shah

('86', 57, 8, 17, 71391) BALVANT SINHA, Knowing you as I do I can say from your remarks that at least for some time you must leave Sevagram.

('86', 57, 8, 28, 71888) It may undergo transformation, as was the case with Sabarmati.
('86', 57, 8, 29, 71951) As long as I am alive and active, there will not be much change at Sevagram.
('86', 57, 8, 30, 72028) I do not wish to make any.
('86', 57, 8, 31, 72055) If I survive, a new order will come in course of time.
('86', 57, 8, 32, 72110) Those who are attached to Sevagram will not give it up for good either now or after I am gone.
('86', 57, 8, 33, 72205) Who can say that after I am dead even Vinoba may not possibly make the place his own?

('86', 57, 8, 35, 72382) I am sure that even though all the organizations are independent, they are unknowingly dependent on Sevagram.
('86', 57, 8, 36, 72492) This is just as well.
('86', 58, 0, 1, 72514) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 59

('86', 61, 5, 10, 76147) 119. LETTER TO RAMDAS GANDHI
('86', 61, 6, 11, 76176) SEVAGRAM, March 18, 1945
('86', 61, 7, 12, 76201) RAMDAS, You form opinions on incomplete information and feel unhappy.
('86', 61, 7, 13, 76271) This has been your old habit.
('86', 61, 7, 14, 76301) You must get rid of it.
('86', 61, 7, 15, 76325) What wrong notions you have formed on the basis of Su[shila]behns letter !
('86', 61, 7, 16, 76400) I am not a person to waste myself physically and mentally.
('86', 61, 7, 17, 76459) I do my work and am happy.
('86', 61, 7, 18, 76486) I put my idea of education into practice in my own case.
('86', 61, 7, 19, 76543) My fastit could not really be called a fast because I took fruit juicewas purely physical.
('86', 61, 7, 20, 76634) I did not find it unbearable.
('86', 61, 7, 21, 76664) I did not agree to take glucose and so had the feeling of fasting.
('86', 61, 7, 22, 76731) But that was only for a short time, as later on I had to take glucose.
('86', 61, 7, 23, 76802) I can tell you more but this should suffice.
('86', 61, 7, 24, 76847) Bear in mind that I take all possible care of myself.
('86', 61, 7, 25, 76901) I hope Kanam is well.
('86', 61, 7, 26, 76923) He wrote to me that he would be coming to Bombay but would be able to do so only after hisexaminations.
('86', 61, 7, 27, 77027) I do not know whether I shall be there then.
('86', 61, 7, 28, 77072) We shall see.
('86', 61, 7, 29, 77086) I hope Ushi has recovered.

('86', 62, 2, 3, 77384) March 18, 1945
('86', 62, 3, 4, 77399) KRISHNACHANDRA, Has it not been proved that in your case proximity to me does not help in observing brahmacharya?

('86', 62, 6, 11, 77954) 121. LETTER TO KRISHNACHANDRA
('86', 62, 7, 12, 77984) SEVAGRAM, March 18, 1945
('86', 62, 8, 13, 78009) KRISHNACHANDRA, Your long letter betrays your state of mind.
('86', 62, 8, 14, 78070) Is it not right that I should write to you taking what you say to be the complete truth?
('86', 62, 8, 15, 78159) The others who are here do not feel very intensely about brahmacharya.
('86', 62, 8, 16, 78230) You do and so I write about it.
('86', 62, 8, 17, 78262) But in the end you must do as you feel.
('86', 62, 8, 18, 78302) If you do something I say without your heart being in it, you may take it that it will be futile.
('86', 62, 8, 19, 78400) It will be no good at all if you mechanically do what I say.
('86', 62, 8, 20, 78461) What you have written is of course true.
('86', 62, 8, 21, 78502) What does it matter?
('86', 62, 8, 22, 78523) I do consult people after all.
('86', 62, 8, 23, 78554) What is the harmeven if the boys leave?
('86', 62, 8, 24, 78594) There is a lot of work to do.
('86', 62, 8, 25, 78624) After all our principle is just this: whoever is available is fit to be taught and fit also to teach.
('86', 62, 8, 26, 78726) You must not become disheartened.
('86', 62, 9, 27, 78760) Blessings from BAPU

('86', 74, 3, 13, 92218) Deep breathing is essential.

('86', 74, 3, 15, 92303) You can gradually increase it to half an hour.
('86', 74, 3, 16, 92350) Utter Ramanama with every breath you take.
('86', 74, 3, 17, 92393) When doing breathing exercises, you should have fresh air on all sides.
('86', 74, 3, 18, 92465) It would be better to do it in the open.
('86', 74, 3, 19, 92506) You should do it every morning without fail and afterwards at least four times after the food has been digested.
('86', 74, 3, 20, 92619) Breathe in and breathe out.
('86', 74, 3, 21, 92647) This exercise should be taken slowly.
('86', 74, 3, 22, 92685) Do your bowels move properly?
('86', 74, 3, 23, 92715) Are you able to sleep?
('86', 74, 3, 24, 92738) If you do all this carefully you will soon get rid of the cough.

('86', 77, 5, 16, 96817) ANSWER: Soul force is nothing but a manifestation of His power or strength.

('86', 77, 5, 18, 96968) Hence satyagraha is directly connected with soul force.

('86', 77, 7, 21, 97135) We can or shall be immortal or live in death by dying non violently (or by sacrificing ourselves for a noble cause) but not by killing others (or by perpetrating violence).

('86', 78, 2, 22, 99452) I was then a novice trying to find out Truth in all its aspects without then knowing that I was so doing.

('86', 81, 1, 2, 101702) 155. LETTER TO MUNNALAL G. SHAH
('86', 81, 2, 3, 101734) March 21, 1945
('86', 81, 3, 4, 101749) MUNNALAL, You should never conclude from anything that I write that I must have examined every aspect.
('86', 81, 3, 5, 101852) That is for you readers to do.
('86', 81, 3, 6, 101883) I would of course relieve you and put up with whatever hardship follows.
('86', 81, 3, 7, 101956) But the truth is that you ought not to abandon the work you have taken up.
('86', 81, 3, 8, 102031) Man may not abandon his duty any more than the ant can abandon the pot of jaggery.
('86', 81, 3, 9, 102114) We, however, look upon duty not as a pot of jaggery but as a burden.
('86', 81, 3, 10, 102183) Otherwise how dare A. S. so much as suggest that you should leave?
('86', 81, 3, 11, 102250) But that is what happened.
('86', 81, 3, 12, 102277) I like what you say.
('86', 81, 3, 13, 102298) By all means cling to the kitchen and make it a model one.
('86', 81, 3, 14, 102357) It will bring you all the joy and you will get training along with the others.
('86', 81, 3, 15, 102436) The gods will shower flowers and it may be I shall be there to watch.
('86', 81, 3, 16, 102506) Make it an ideal kitchen.
('86', 81, 3, 17, 102532) Run it with the help of servants, so called, but let them feel that they are not servants but masters or trustees.

('86', 81, 3, 20, 102704) Forget Kanchan if possible.

('86', 81, 3, 22, 102802) After both of you have become tempered, you will meet again.
('86', 81, 3, 23, 102863) If you can do this, you will have brought down many fruits with one stone.
('86', 81, 3, 24, 102938) The saying is about killing many birds with one stone.
('86', 81, 3, 25, 102993) That is a wrong one, ours is the right one.
('86', 81, 4, 26, 103037) Blessings from BAPU

('86', 89, 1, 2, 110971) 174. LETTER TO MANAHAR
('86', 89, 2, 3, 110994) SEVAGRAM, March 23, 1945
('86', 89, 3, 4, 111019) BHAI MANAHAR1, I discovered only today that the money for Shastrijis 2
('86', 89, 4, 5, 111090) maintenance was being sent from here.
('86', 89, 4, 6, 111128) The expenditure in my opinion is too high.
('86', 89, 4, 7, 111171) All expenditure should be channelled through you.
('86', 89, 4, 8, 111221) I find even rent included in the expenses.
('86', 89, 4, 9, 111264) The amount of Rs. 100 was sent to cover four months but almost the whole amount was spent in three months.
('86', 89, 4, 10, 111371) I am also enclosing Shastrijis letter.
('86', 89, 4, 11, 111410) Tell me after looking into everything how much should be paid.
('86', 89, 4, 12, 111473) I do not have any private money of my own.
('86', 89, 4, 13, 111516) Whatever I have is from donations.
('86', 89, 4, 14, 111551) Surely I cannot make donations out of donations.
('86', 89, 4, 15, 111600) I can spend money only for the purpose for which the donations are meant.
('86', 89, 4, 16, 111674) The money paid to your account depends on donations.
('86', 89, 4, 17, 111727) Please let me know how much I should give for Shastriji.
('86', 89, 4, 18, 111784) Whatever is done should be through you.
('86', 89, 4, 19, 111824) Consider Shastriji to be your patient.
('86', 89, 4, 20, 111863) He can see this letter.
('86', 89, 5, 21, 111887) Blessings from BAPU [PS.] I am not talking about the past.
('86', 89, 5, 22, 111946) I say that there should be some restriction now.
('86', 89, 5, 23, 111995) Shastriji is ill.
('86', 89, 5, 24, 112013) He cannot even think properly.
('86', 89, 5, 25, 112044) Whatever has to be done must be done either by you or by me.
('86', 89, 5, 26, 112105) I can do nothing from here and so it becomes your duty.
('86', 89, 5, 27, 112161) You must tell me how much should be sent to you.
('86', 89, 5, 28, 112210) Shastriji has to be placed under your control.

('86', 94, 2, 3, 116559) March 24, 1945 Personality, i.e., the quality of being oneself, can be good or bad.
('86', 94, 2, 4, 116643) If it is in conformity with the Self it is good and if it disregards the Self it is bad.
('86', 94, 2, 5, 116732) It becomes good and develops by meditating on the Self and understanding its attributes.

('86', 94, 5, 8, 116882) 186. SPEECH AT A. I. S. A. MEETING I2
('86', 94, 6, 9, 116920) SEVAGRAM, March 24, 1945 I regret I shall not be able to be present throughout the entire proceedings.
('86', 94, 6, 10, 117023) The reason is that I wish to live for 125 years, so that I can serve the country longer.
('86', 94, 6, 11, 117112) I was not joking when I said so at the August meeting of A. I. C. C., for a satyagrahi never utters a word that he does not mean.
('86', 94, 6, 12, 117242) I earnestly endeavour to fulfil this wish of mine and to this end I try to conserve as much of my energy as I can.
('86', 94, 6, 13, 117357) Whether I succeed in my desire to live to 125 years will not depend on doctors or medical science, though in my own way I have used the aid of both a good deal.
('86', 94, 6, 14, 117518) It will depend on my ability fully to translate into practice the principles of truth and ahimsa.
('86', 94, 6, 15, 117616) My experience of ahimsa has taught me that even in the work of service the pace should not be too fast.
('86', 94, 6, 16, 117720) I confess that in this I have been only partially successful.
('86', 94, 6, 17, 117782) I cannot regulate my pace sufficiently.
('86', 94, 6, 18, 117822) Old, settled habits are not overcome all at once.
('86', 94, 6, 19, 117872) I know undue haste is bad; it impedes work instead of facilitating it.
('86', 94, 6, 20, 117943) I have been asked whether it is desirable to mix politics and constructive work.
('86', 94, 6, 21, 118024) At present some people are doing constructive workin order to strengthen the Congress organization.
('86', 94, 6, 22, 118124) This mixing of

('86', 95, 1, 2, 118394) politics and constructive work helps neither.
('86', 95, 1, 3, 118440) I entirely concur with the view that for full justice to be done to constructive work it must stand on its own feet and should not be tied to political work.
('86', 95, 1, 4, 118598) I fear this advice of mine will not have any effect.
('86', 95, 1, 5, 118651) But as the author of the Mahabharata says, You must continue to proclaim the truth irrespective of whether anybody listens to you or not. This comforts me.
('86', 95, 1, 6, 118807) Since I first presented through the Congress the constructive programme to the country in 1920, my faith in its efficacy has become stronger.
('86', 95, 1, 7, 118949) In the light of experience and knowledge gained, its scope has been enlarged.
('86', 95, 1, 8, 119027) It is my claim, and I have proclaimed it from the house tops, that my 15 point programme is comprehensive and if it is pursued throughout the country we shall gain swaraj without any other programme.
('86', 95, 2, 9, 119227) Mahatma Gandhi referred to the formation of the Congress Ministry in the North West Frontier Province and the reported efforts of Mr. Bhulabhai Desai to end the political deadlock and said: 1
('86', 95, 3, 10, 119419) I prefer to keep silent on these points for the present.
('86', 95, 3, 11, 119476) The Parliamentary programme may result in political swaraj; but non violent swaraj is possible only by fully implementing the constructive programme.
('86', 95, 4, 12, 119626) If only the constructive programme was worked in the right spirit, there was no need either to incur the wrath of the ruling race or even to enter the Legislatures.
('86', 95, 4, 13, 119791) But Gandhiji urged that even if parliamentary work was permitted, the special importance of the constructive programme would always remain and through it alone the freedom of the country could be achieved.
('86', 95, 4, 14, 119997) It may be asked whether the people will take up the constructive programme and pursue it in the way I want it pursued.
('86', 95, 4, 15, 120116) My answer is that whether they do so or not does not take away from the merit of the remedy I advocate which is both good and practicable.
('86', 95, 4, 16, 120255) In this connection I have been asked whether, since carrying on of the movement against untouchability and organizing of peasants and workers in the name of the Congress provides a chance to Ambedkar and others to raise opposition and thus impede anti untouchability work, it would not be better if these programmes were pursued independently of the Congress.
('86', 95, 4, 17, 120615) It is my view that if the followers of Ambedkar oppose us we
('86', 95, 5, 18, 120676) 1 This and the two following paragraphs are from The Hindu.
('86', 96, 0, 1, 120736) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 97
('86', 96, 1, 2, 120776) should not let ourselves be provoked or give up our work because of it.
('86', 96, 1, 3, 120848) We should reach their hearts and understand their feelings.
('86', 96, 1, 4, 120908) If we had gone through the experiences that the Harijans have gone through, there is no telling how embittered we might not have become and how little our ahimsa would have endured.
('86', 96, 1, 5, 121090) Therefore on such occasions we should look inward and if there is the slightest vestige of untouchability left we should purge ourselves of it.
('86', 96, 1, 6, 121234) It is my firm belief that if Hinduism is to survive, untouchability must go.
('86', 96, 1, 7, 121311) If untouchability lives, Hinduism is bound to perish and will deserve to perish.
('86', 96, 1, 8, 121392) The tragedy is that those who should have especially devoted themselves to the work of reform did not put their hearts into the thing and only played with it.
('86', 96, 1, 9, 121551) What wonder that Harijan brethren feel suspicious, and show opposition and bitterness?
('86', 96, 1, 10, 121638) The removal of untouchability root and branch thus becomes a religious duty for me and for other Hindus like me.
('86', 96, 1, 11, 121751) If we want to achieve swaraj through non violence then untouchability will have to be eradicated.
('86', 96, 1, 12, 121849) We cannot attain swaraj without that.
('86', 96, 1, 13, 121887) Not all Congressmen share this view of mine.
('86', 96, 1, 14, 121932) The Cangress is a democratic organization and it can have in it people representing many points of view.
('86', 96, 1, 15, 122037) No one has the right to thrust his own view on others and expect them to work in pursuance of those views.
('86', 96, 1, 16, 122144) It will be right if those who consider eradication of untouchability a religious duty give themselves up exclusively to this work with single minded devotion.
('86', 96, 1, 17, 122303) At the same time it will also be right if those who consider anti untouchability work as a part of the political programme of the Congress pursue it as such.
('86', 96, 1, 18, 122461) Religious duty is a very subtle and complicated thing.
('86', 96, 1, 19, 122516) It is not a commodity that can be bought and sold.
('86', 96, 1, 20, 122567) Perpetual inner searching is needed in order to discover it.
('86', 96, 1, 21, 122628) In essence it is the same for all times and all places but its form and its translation into practice changes from individual to individual and from time to time.
('86', 96, 1, 22, 122791) If we can but grasp this secret of the many sidedness of truth we shall be able to see any differences between principles and practice in their proper perspective.
('86', 96, 1, 23, 122955) I therefore welcome both those who work for the eradication of untouchability independently and those who do so in pursuance of the Congress programme.
('86', 96, 2, 24, 123107) The same argument, he said, applied to the question whether Congressmen

('86', 97, 1, 4, 123359) He said he had already informed Mr. N. G. Ranga that it would lead to conflict if there was a separate organization for peasants and workers and consequent weakening of both the organizations.
('86', 97, 2, 5, 123552) He himself had ceased to be a four anna member of the Congress and yet he claimed that he was rendering more service to the Congress by remaining outside.

('86', 97, 3, 8, 123986) Gandhiji concluded the first set of questions by repeating what he had often said before that he was there merely to advise.
('86', 97, 3, 9, 124111) No one was bound to accept his advice unless it appealed to his head and heart.
('86', 97, 3, 10, 124191) The other question asked is whether the funds of the Charkha Sangh can be used for giving training to khadi workers in other branches of constructive work, such as agriculture, animal husbandry and Nayee Talim, in order to equip them for allround village service.
('86', 97, 3, 11, 124455) My answer is no.
('86', 97, 3, 12, 124472) Funds collected for one institution cannot be spent on another.
('86', 97, 3, 13, 124536) According to the constitution of the Charkha Sangh its funds cannot be used for any purpose other than khadi.
('86', 97, 3, 14, 124646) Therefore expenditure on training in agriculture and animal husbandry should be borne by the institution concerned.
('86', 97, 3, 15, 124762) Otherwise it will lead to confusion.

('86', 97, 3, 17, 124963) The job of a trustee is difficult and dedicate.
('86', 97, 3, 18, 125011) I have been atrustee of various institutions for over fifty years and every institution under me has flourished.
('86', 97, 3, 19, 125124) The secret of my success is not my Mahatmaship but my business sense and the meticulous care I show in maintaining accounts.
('86', 97, 3, 20, 125249) The success or otherwise of a public institution ought not to depend on the brilliance of an individual or individuals but on the purity of its management and the soundness of its business policy.
('86', 97, 3, 21, 125446) If you cultivate these money will come to you of itself.
('86', 97, 3, 22, 125503) A friend has suggested that khadi work instead of being carried on through the various branches of the Charkha Sangh should, within a specified time, be entrusted to workers engaged in all round village work who understand the scheme.
('86', 97, 3, 23, 125738) I agree with the suggestion, but I am not in favour of laying down a time limit for winding up all khadi production activity.

('86', 98, 2, 23, 128093) He was happy that with infinite patience they had achieved something in spite of their slavery and other obstacles, and he was really proud of the achievement.

('86', 99, 1, 2, 128606) 187. MESSAGE ON DEATH OF HERMANN KALLENBACH1
('86', 99, 2, 3, 128651) SEVAGRAM, March 25, 1945 South Africa has lost a most generous minded citizen and the Indians of that subcontinent a very warm friend.
('86', 99, 2, 4, 128786) In Hermann Kallenbachs death I have lost a very dear and near friend.
('86', 99, 2, 5, 128856) He used to say to me often that when I was deserted by the whole world, I would find him to be a true friend going with me, if need be, to the ends of the earth in search of Truth.
('86', 99, 2, 6, 129037) He used to spend at one time 75 per month on his person alone.
('86', 99, 2, 7, 129100) But he so revolutionized his life that his monthly personal expenses amounted to under 8. This lasted while we lived together in a cottage seven miles from Johannesburg.
('86', 99, 2, 8, 129270) When I left South Africa, he reverted in large part to his original life though mostly eschewing the things of life he had deliberately left.
('86', 99, 2, 9, 129412) He came in close touch with the late patriot Mr. G. K. Gokhale, who held him in high esteem.
('86', 99, 2, 10, 129505) It may be noted that together with Henry Polak, Mr. H. Kallenbach was arrested for marching with me from Natal to Transvaal 2. The Hindu, 27 3 1945

('86', 101, 0, 1, 131565) 102 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('86', 101, 1, 2, 131607) 191. SPEECH AT A. I. S. A. MEETINGII
('86', 101, 2, 3, 131644) SEVAGRAM, March 25, 1945 Jajuji says that the quantity of yarn tendered in partial payment for khadi should be increased from two pice to 2_ as., or a hank of yarn per rupee.
('86', 101, 2, 4, 131819) This is too mild.
('86', 101, 2, 5, 131837) I would go further.
('86', 101, 2, 6, 131857) Some days back Bombay had become the Manchester of khadi.
('86', 101, 2, 7, 131915) Khadi was brought from far and wide and sold there.
('86', 101, 2, 8, 131967) The credit for this went to the salesmanship of Shri Vithaldas Jerajani.
('86', 101, 2, 9, 132040) It was thanks to his efforts that first swadeshi goods and then khadi entered Bombay.
('86', 101, 2, 10, 132126) But now I see that that was not the light way.
('86', 101, 2, 11, 132173) Khadi, in the first place, should be consumed where it is produced.
('86', 101, 2, 12, 132241) If in a particular place khadi in excess of the requirement is produced the surplus should be sent to the nearest place where it is needed.
('86', 101, 2, 13, 132381) The district should be the limit or at most the province.
('86', 101, 2, 14, 132439) Indeed I would not go even as far as the province.
('86', 101, 2, 15, 132490) A district is a large enough area for this sort of transaction.
('86', 101, 2, 16, 132554) The aim of course is that the khadi produced in a village should be sold in that village.
('86', 101, 2, 17, 132644) But out of the seven lakh villages in India how many are there which can make this claim about themselves?
('86', 101, 2, 18, 132751) In the villages where khadi is produced the spinners and weavers, for all the efforts of the Charkha Sangh, use very little of the khadi they produce.
('86', 101, 2, 19, 132902) This is against the ideal of khadi.
('86', 101, 2, 20, 132938) The condition of two pice per rupee to be tendered in yarn for the purchase of khadi does not apply to villagers.
('86', 101, 2, 21, 133052) They must sell khadi only in exchange of yarn.
('86', 101, 2, 22, 133099) Do you fear that if you enforce the yarn condition the sale of khadi in cities will suffer?
('86', 101, 2, 23, 133191) If you do not get rid of this fear you will kill khadi.
('86', 101, 3, 24, 133247) The rule of giving half an anna worth of yarn for one rupee of khadi purchased is generally meant for big cities and I would desire that all should spin and produce their khadi.
('86', 101, 3, 25, 133425) Khadi is the emblem oftruth and non violence.
('86', 101, 3, 26, 133471) Such exchange of yarn may result in reducing the number of khadi wearers but we should carry on our work in that direction and ultimately we shall succeed.
('86', 101, 3, 27, 133627) Khadi has won a place of honour in society.
('86', 101, 3, 28, 133671) The rich feel proud of buying khadi produced by the poor.
('86', 101, 3, 29, 133729) But this is not enough.
('86', 101, 3, 30, 133753) If you limit the role of khadi to providing bread to the poor, it cannot be an
('86', 101, 4, 31, 133832) 1 The following paragraph is from The Hitavada, 27 3 1945.
('86', 102, 0, 1, 133891) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 103
('86', 102, 1, 2, 133932) instrument for securing swaraj through non violence.
('86', 102, 1, 3, 133985) I do not want this.
('86', 102, 1, 4, 134005) Even if I were the only one left to buy khadi on condition of yarn being tendered I should not worry.
('86', 102, 1, 5, 134107) You have accepted khadi as the symbol of non violence.
('86', 102, 1, 6, 134162) You have also accepted it as the means for securing swaraj.
('86', 102, 1, 7, 134222) If it is the will of God that khadi should die I would rather it died a natural death than that your timidity and lack of faith should be the cause of its demise.
('86', 102, 1, 8, 134385) Those who for some reason cannot themselves spin can get their wives, mothers, sisters or servants to spin.
('86', 102, 1, 9, 134493) Failing that they may get yarn from their neighbours but not on payment.
('86', 102, 2, 10, 134566) Next he produced some figures 2 which Shri Aryanayakum and Smt.
('86', 102, 2, 11, 134630) Asha Devi had given him.
('86', 102, 2, 12, 134655) He considered those figures to be most revealing.
('86', 102, 2, 13, 134705) They were proof positive of how quickly khadi could be introduced in the villages through Nayee Talim.
('86', 102, 2, 14, 134808) Cloth produced by the children during the period of their training would be sufficient to cloth the entire village and it would be the cheapest cloth possible.
('86', 102, 2, 15, 134968) We should increase our love for khadi and serve the villages.
('86', 102, 2, 16, 135030) You should make all your dependents khadi wearers.
('86', 102, 2, 17, 135081) I have compared khadi to the sun and the other industries to the planets in the solar system.
('86', 102, 2, 18, 135175) Agriculture is a planet in this solar system but it cannot be the sun, for agriculture is not free.
('86', 102, 2, 19, 135275) Those who till the land do not own it.
('86', 102, 2, 20, 135314) The Government controls it through petty officials.
('86', 102, 2, 21, 135366) The people have lost self confidence.
('86', 102, 2, 22, 135404) Harmful customs have led to fragmentation of land.
('86', 102, 2, 23, 135455) If I am alive fifty years hence and if by that time people have gained control of the land I shall reconsider its place in my solar system.
('86', 102, 2, 24, 135595) I can say that agriculture by itself cannot develop the intellect as much as khadi and other village industries can.
('86', 102, 2, 25, 135712) As the late Madhusudan once said, constant company of bullocks turns men into bullocks.
('86', 102, 2, 26, 135800) The gist of what I have told you during the past two days is that if you have faith in my ideal you should put your whole effort behind it.
('86', 102, 2, 27, 135940) The Shastras proclaim that Truth ever triumphs.
('86', 102, 2, 28, 135988) This is a universally valid principle.
('86', 102, 2, 29, 136027) If sometimes in life it is seen to fail the reason is not that the principle is at fault.
('86', 102, 2, 30, 136117) It shows the imperfection of the man who is applying the principle.
('86', 102, 2, 31, 136185) Once you have understood the principle you will have developed that detachment and that freedom

('86', 103, 3, 6, 136719) 192. ANSWERS TO QUESTIONS1
('86', 103, 4, 7, 136746) March 25, 1945
('86', 103, 5, 8, 136761) Q. 1. Some members of the Charkha Sangh took a leading part in sabotage activities.
('86', 103, 5, 9, 136845) .The Government became suspicious and took represssive measures against such organizations.
('86', 103, 5, 10, 136937) In such a situation, is it not a mistake to put the entire blame on the Government?
('86', 103, 6, 11, 137021) A. Just because some worker went astray, it was wrong to punish the Charkha Sangh.
('86', 103, 6, 12, 137104) I blame the Government entirely for its high handedness.
('86', 103, 7, 13, 137161) Q. 2. Some Congressmen whose faith in non violence was not very strong ...
('86', 103, 7, 14, 137236) are full of ideas regarding sabotage.
('86', 103, 7, 15, 137274) How can these people be weaned away from these ideas?
('86', 103, 8, 16, 137328) A. Those who have lost faith in non violence will recover it through the work of the people who have retained their faith.
('86', 103, 8, 17, 137451) They will never recover it through reprimands.
('86', 103, 8, 18, 137498) They are following their own convictions.
('86', 103, 8, 19, 137540) Let us be perfect as they are imperfect Darkness is dispelled by the rising of the sun.
('86', 103, 9, 20, 137628) Q. 3. These days the committees for constructive work appointed by the Congress are full of people with the ideas mentioned in question No.
('86', 103, 9, 21, 137768) 2. There are some devoted people too.
('86', 103, 9, 22, 137806) Do you believe that the constructive work can make progress with the help of such committees?
('86', 103, 10, 23, 137900) A. The constructive work will proceed if the people having faith can give expression to their faith not through words but through deeds.
('86', 103, 11, 24, 138037) Q. 4. Under such circumstances, would it not be better that the people having faith in non violence should carry on their work independently of others?
('86', 103, 12, 25, 138189) A. The answer is contained in the previous answers and also in my speech.
('86', 103, 13, 26, 138263) 1 The questions were from Pundalik Katagde.
('86', 103, 13, 27, 138307) 2 Vide Speech at A. I. S. A. Meeting I, 24 3 1945.
('86', 104, 0, 1, 138358) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 105
('86', 104, 1, 2, 138399) Q. 5. Those who have no faith in non violence and, for that reason, are not able to contribute to the programme based on non violence are in a very uncomfortable position in the constructive work committees.
('86', 104, 1, 3, 138607) This has a demoralizing effect on them.
('86', 104, 1, 4, 138647) In such a situation would it not be proper to let their efforts find scope in Parliamentary activities?
('86', 104, 2, 5, 138751) A. Do we restrict anyone from going into the Parliament?
('86', 104, 2, 6, 138808) It is enough that we do not go ourselves.
('86', 104, 3, 7, 138850) Q. 6. Will there not be greater scope for basic education, stopping corruption, improving the food situation, removing the difficulties of the villagers and so on, if the Congress assumes power?
('86', 104, 4, 8, 139045) A. It may or may not happen.
('86', 104, 4, 9, 139074) It will depend on what type of people come forward and on the state of public opinion.
('86', 104, 5, 10, 139161) Q. 7....
('86', 104, 5, 11, 139170) Can I give my opinion in favour of bringing electricity to the villages, particularly in Hudli?
('86', 104, 6, 12, 139266) A. I am strongly opposed to it.
('86', 104, 6, 13, 139298) My answers are not meant for publication.
('86', 104, 6, 14, 139340) Yon can show them to friends.
('86', 104, 7, 15, 139370) BAPU [PS.] I have not revised this.
('86', 104, 7, 16, 139406) Correct the slips yourself or get them corrected.
('86', 104, 8, 17, 139456) From a photostat of the Hindi: G.N. 5227

('86', 106, 6, 14, 140986) 197. LETTER TO MUNNALAL G. SHAH
('86', 106, 7, 15, 141018) [March 26, 1945] 1
('86', 106, 8, 16, 141037) MUNNALAL, Here is for your guidance.
('86', 106, 8, 17, 141074) There must be rules, and they must be obeyed.
('86', 106, 8, 18, 141120) Manage somehow during these five days.
('86', 106, 8, 19, 141159) Then after my return we shall see.
('86', 106, 8, 20, 141194) I am in favour of two kitchens.
('86', 106, 8, 21, 141226) If I were in your place, I would attend to everything you mention and do it well.
('86', 106, 8, 22, 141308) I have done that.
('86', 106, 8, 23, 141326) But that does not mean that, your doing what I would have done will necessarily bear fruit.
('86', 106, 8, 24, 141418) There is no such rule.
('86', 106, 8, 25, 141441) You may act as you like, but on one condition, namely, that you must be absolutely sure that you are following truth and ahimsa.
('86', 106, 8, 26, 141570) If the persons you have named do not observe the rules, you should talk to them one by one and find out why.
('86', 106, 8, 27, 141679) If a person admits the fact, you may make an exception in his favour, and if you find that the exceptions are so many that they defeat the rule you should revise the rule.
('86', 106, 8, 28, 141851) I understand from what you write that the exceptions do defeat the rule.
('86', 106, 8, 29, 141924) This isindeed a hotel.
('86', 106, 8, 30, 141947) But it is more than that.
('86', 106, 8, 31, 141973) A hotel is a place where
('86', 106, 9, 32, 141998) 1 The addressees letter, to which this is a reply, was delivered to Gandhiji at 5.15 a.

('86', 106, 9, 34, 142143) on March 26.

('86', 107, 1, 2, 142198) people pay for boarding and lodging.
('86', 107, 1, 3, 142235) They order and get whatever they want, and feel no embarrassment.
('86', 107, 1, 4, 142301) It should be so here also.
('86', 107, 1, 5, 142328) Here, too, we must have some rules, as every hotel has.
('86', 107, 1, 6, 142384) For instance, we would serve no non vegetarian food or cater to peoples taste in regard to spices.
('86', 107, 1, 7, 142483) Let Shakaribehn start a separate kitchen.
('86', 107, 1, 8, 142525) Anybody else who wishes may also do that.
('86', 107, 1, 9, 142567) Meet every permanent resident and know from him or her their wishes, then frame rules and get them passed in the presence of all and see that everyone observes the rule which he himself has accepted.
('86', 107, 1, 10, 142767) I knew about Kamle today by chance.

('86', 107, 1, 22, 143352) About the spoon I am not convinced.
('86', 107, 1, 23, 143388) Two bowls may be all right, though I am not sure.
('86', 107, 1, 24, 143438) Serving ghee with the vegetable will not do.
('86', 107, 1, 25, 143483) Perhaps it will not do even to put it on the chapatis.
('86', 107, 1, 26, 143538) If the vegetable is served in a bowl, ghee may be added to it.
('86', 107, 1, 27, 143601) But I have seen only one bowl in many places.
('86', 107, 1, 28, 143647) I am giving no ruling in this matter.
('86', 107, 1, 29, 143685) Personally, I would provide only one bowl.
('86', 107, 1, 30, 143728) But I give no ruling.

('86', 108, 1, 2, 144335) 198. LETTER TO MUNNALAL G. SHAH March 26, 1945
('86', 108, 2, 3, 144382) MUNNALAL, It would be better if the thing was done before I left for Bombay.
('86', 108, 2, 4, 144459) 1 But do not sacrifice your sleep for that.
('86', 108, 2, 5, 144503) I was glad that the problem about Sushilabehn had been solved.
('86', 108, 2, 6, 144566) My success holds no lesson for anybody, but it may give one hope.
('86', 108, 2, 7, 144632) There may be many reasons for my success.
('86', 108, 2, 8, 144674) According to me, the chief reason is my ahimsa.
('86', 108, 2, 9, 144722) From your point of view it is true that your training has not fitted you for managing a kitchen.
('86', 108, 2, 10, 144819) When you learn non attachment you will not say that.
('86', 108, 2, 11, 144872) We are fit enough for any duty that comes to us unsought.
('86', 108, 2, 12, 144930) The secret is that we do not run after any task; the task comes to us unsought.
('86', 108, 2, 13, 145010) If you look upon a servant as your own brother or sister, you will never fail.
('86', 108, 2, 14, 145089) Yesterday the kedgeree was not well cooked.
('86', 108, 2, 15, 145133) Manu refused to eat it and so I examined it with my fingers.
('86', 108, 2, 16, 145194) Finding that it was insufficiently cooked I made her a sign that she need not eat it.
('86', 108, 2, 17, 145280) If I had insisted, she would have consumed it and suffered from stomachache in consequence.
('86', 108, 2, 18, 145372) If everybody had eaten it that would have been no evidence that it was well cooked.
('86', 108, 2, 19, 145456) I explained to Kalukhan himself about Magandeep.
('86', 108, 2, 20, 145505) I understand about Aundh.
('86', 108, 2, 21, 145531) I think nothing remains now.
('86', 108, 2, 22, 145560) Blessings from BAPU [PS.] Instead of engraving peoples names on the utensils, they should be numbered.
('86', 108, 2, 23, 145663) This is the practice in jails, as also in institutions.
('86', 108, 2, 24, 145719) Instead of purchasing additional utensils, find some way out.
('86', 108, 2, 25, 145781) In the last resort, we can always have [leaf cups] 2. If you can have inexpensive earthen ones you may have them.
('86', 108, 2, 26, 145895) Everybody may make for himself spoons of wood.
('86', 108, 2, 27, 145942) We can teach them.
('86', 108, 2, 28, 145961) It is quite easy to learn.
('86', 108, 2, 29, 145988) Think what the poor would do and find some way.
('86', 108, 2, 30, 146036) Discuss the matter with the permanent residents.
('86', 108, 2, 31, 146085) Mohan Singh will probably suggest something.
('86', 108, 2, 32, 146130) Moreover, now I shall be leaving, so you will have no difficulty during that time.
('86', 108, 2, 33, 146213) Think over the matter before I return.
('86', 108, 2, 34, 146252) You can certainly make wooden ones.
('86', 108, 2, 35, 146288) We used to do that in S. A. The wood and the knife were supplied by the jail authorities.

('86', 112, 6, 10, 150117) 207. LETTER TO MUNNALAL G. SHAH
('86', 112, 7, 11, 150149) March 27, 1945
('86', 112, 8, 12, 150164) MUNNALAL, One must try to get rid of whatever bad habit one recognizes in oneself.
('86', 112, 8, 13, 150247) Your pen runs independently of you.
('86', 112, 8, 14, 150283) Discipline it and then let it climb a hill.
('86', 112, 8, 15, 150327) I can only indicate the ideal.
('86', 112, 8, 16, 150358) It is for you to reach it or not.
('86', 112, 8, 17, 150392) How can I say that you can do so much and no more?
('86', 112, 8, 18, 150443) I shall try to adjust myself to you as much as I can.
('86', 112, 8, 19, 150497) Perhaps there is no spare pair of sandals.
('86', 112, 8, 20, 150540) You will get the loin cloth.
('86', 112, 8, 21, 150569) It cannot be called a lungi.
('86', 112, 8, 22, 150598) A lungi cannot be tucked up from behind.
('86', 112, 8, 23, 150639) Bhansali and Balkrishna wear lungis.
('86', 112, 8, 24, 150676) Give up hope of sandals.
('86', 112, 8, 25, 150701) I have no spare pair at all.
('86', 112, 8, 26, 150730) About the books, after my return.
('86', 112, 8, 27, 150764) Use the ones which are lying with me.

('86', 130, 0, 1, 171145) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 131
('86', 130, 1, 2, 171186) 248. STATEMENT TO THE PRESS
('86', 130, 2, 3, 171214) BOMBAY, March 31, 1945 The National Week 1 will be presently on us.
('86', 130, 2, 4, 171282) We began to observe the Week in 1919. We had the unexpected and spontaneous manifestation of the villagers all over India.
('86', 130, 2, 5, 171405) Seven days after, Jallianwala Bagh massacre, also unthought of, took place.
('86', 130, 2, 6, 171481) We have observed the Week ever since in triple expectation of achieving communal unity, full establishment of khaddar and swaraj.
('86', 130, 2, 7, 171611) We seemed to be at one time within an ace of the triple achievement.
('86', 130, 2, 8, 171680) But today we seem to be very far.
('86', 130, 2, 9, 171714) I advisedly use the verb seem.
('86', 130, 2, 10, 171745) The goal ever seems to recede from us but if we have honestly worked for it, it really comes nearer.
('86', 130, 2, 11, 171846) Anyhow I feel so.
('86', 130, 2, 12, 171864) We were never nearer the goal than now in spite of our many blunders.
('86', 130, 2, 13, 171934) It is as well that we remember our blunders and fail to notice the successes lying underneath.
('86', 130, 2, 14, 172029) Only our blunders must never dishearten us.
('86', 130, 2, 15, 172073) We must learn to profit by them and correct them.
('86', 130, 2, 16, 172123) Then every blunder will hearten us, for we shall mount a step higher by unlearning each blunder.
('86', 130, 2, 17, 172220) Thus it becomes a cleansing process.
('86', 130, 2, 18, 172257) Let it be noted that khaddar has attained a wider connotation than before.
('86', 130, 2, 19, 172332) It has become the central sun round which other village industries revolve like so many planets.
('86', 130, 2, 20, 172429) Moreover it now represents the fifteenfold constructive programme.
('86', 130, 2, 21, 172496) Khaddar itself has after much experience got its proper value and thus has received a dignity never before given to it.
('86', 130, 2, 22, 172616) Everyone is now able, with the introduction by Vinoba of tunar 2 to make his or her punis 3 and spin with ease.
('86', 130, 2, 23, 172728) The wheel too has undergone radical improvement and the new process of doubling yarn has made it as strong as one could wish for weaving.
('86', 130, 2, 24, 172866) Would that every lover of freedom of India will remember these things during the Week and bring freedom nearer than ever before without parliamentary programme and even civil disobedience unless the Government drive workers to it by talking of Indias freedom without meaning it.
('86', 130, 2, 25, 173145) The Bombay Chronicle, 1 4 1945
('86', 130, 3, 26, 173176) 1 From April 6 to April 13 2 Carding brush 3 Slivers
('86', 131, 0, 1, 173229) 132 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('86', 131, 1, 2, 173271) 249. STATEMENT TO THE PRESS
('86', 131, 2, 3, 173299) BOMBAY, March 31, 1945 If the news is correct that the Ashti and Chimur petition has been rejected, it is disturbing.
('86', 131, 2, 4, 173417) 1 I am opposed to State hanging in every case, but most so in cases like these.
('86', 131, 2, 5, 173497) Whatever was done by the people on and after August 9, 1942, was done under excitement.
('86', 131, 2, 6, 173585) If these hangings are now carried out, it will be cold blooded, calculated murder and worse, because it will be done ceremoniously and under the name of so called law.
('86', 131, 2, 7, 173753) It will leave behind nothing but a great increase in the already existing woeful bitterness.
('86', 131, 2, 8, 173846) How I wish that the threatened hangings were given up.
('86', 131, 2, 9, 173901) They can be if there is the united voice of India against the impending sentences and such other contemplated sentences.
('86', 131, 2, 10, 174022) The Hindu, 1 4 1945

('86', 132, 1, 2, 174768) 251. DRAFT OF POWER OF ATTORNEY
('86', 132, 2, 3, 174800) April 1, 1945 To all to whom these presents shall come, we Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi, Sir Purshottamdas Thakurdas, Sir Sarvapalli Radhakrishnan, Dr. Kailas Nath Katju, Kasturbhai Lalbhai, Lady Premlila Vithaldas Thackersey, Kanhaiyalal Manecklal Munshi, Devdas Gandhi, Ghanshyamdas Birla, Chakravarti C. Rajagopal achariar, Jehangir R. D. Tata, Sarojini Naidu, Dr. Zakir Hussain, Amritlal Vithaldas Thakkar, Shantikumar Narottam Morarjee, Ambalal Sarabhai, Jankidevi Bajaj, Ashadevi Aryanayakum, Miss Mridula Sarabhai, Miss Raihana Tyabji, Mrs. Gosibehn Captain, Mangaldas Manchram Pakvasa, Ganesh Vasudeo Mavalankar, Shri Krishna Das Mulchand Jaju, Babu Lakshminarayan of Patna, and Gulzarilal Nanda, the present trustees of the Kasturba Gandhi National Memorial Trust hereinafter referred to as the Trustees send greeting whereas by a Deed of Settlement dated the 1st day of April 1945 made between the said Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi of the One Part and the Trustees of the Other Part, the Trustees are appointed Trustees of the Kasturba Gandhi National Memorial Trust (hereinafter for brevitys sake called The Trust) AND WHEREAS in the Court of administration and management of The Trust, the Trustees will be required to deal with immoveable and moveable properties and for such purposes will have to execute documents some of which may also require registration and whereas it is not convenient for the Trustees to go to different places where documents are to be executed and/or registered and to present the same for registration and/or admit execution of the documents that may be executed by us as such trustees of the Trust from time to time and attend before any Registrar or Sub Registrar as the case may be for the purpose aforesaid, we are desirous of appointing Mangaldas Pakvasa, Shantikumar Narottam Morarjee and Shyamlalji, hereinafter called the attorneys to be the true and lawful attorneys on our behalf as also on behalf of any one or more of us, to do all or any of the following acts deeds and things: NOW KNOW YE AND THESE PRESENT WITNESS that we, the Trustees of the said Trust do hereby nominate, constitute the said Mangaldas Pakvasa, Shantikumar Narottam Morarjee and Shyamlalji jointly and severally, i.e., any one of them to be our attorneys for us and in our name to do the following acts and things.1. To execute for
('86', 133, 0, 1, 177152) 134 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('86', 133, 1, 2, 177194) and/or on behalf of the Trustees such documents as they may ressolve upon to execute and/or to appear before the Registrar or Sub Registrar of Assurances and present and/or admit execution of any document or documents or writing that may be or may have been signed or executed by us for any one or more of us or to which we or anyone or more of us may be any parties or party as such Trustees of the Trust and to do all things that may be required or found necessary for procuring the registration thereof as the attorney or attorneys shall think necessary.
('86', 133, 1, 3, 177752) 2. For the better doing, performing and executing of the matters and things aforesaid we hereby further grant unto the said attorneys authority to substitute and appoint in his/their place and stead one or more attorney or attorneys to exercise for ourselves as our attorneys or attorney any or all the powers and authorities hereby conferred and to revoke any such appointment from time to time and to substitute or appoint any other or others in the place of such attorney or attorneys as they the said attorneys shall from time to time think fit.
('86', 133, 1, 4, 178302) 3. We hereby undertake to ratify whatsoever the attorneys or any of them or any substitute or substitutes shall lawfully do or cause to be done in the premises and to indemnify them and each of them against all costs and expenses properly incurred by them or any of them hereunder.

('86', 135, 1, 2, 180455) 254. LETTER TO MANZAR ALI SOKHTA
('86', 135, 2, 3, 180488) BOMBAY , April 1, 1945
('86', 135, 3, 4, 180511) BHAI MANZAR ALI, What I have been told about women seems right.
('86', 135, 3, 5, 180575) The thing is that they should do something or other and they should not lag behind men in doing any work for the country.

('86', 139, 6, 15, 186028) 264. SPEECH AT PRAYER MEETING1
('86', 139, 7, 16, 186059) BOMBAY, April 3, 1945
('86', 139, 8, 17, 186081) Gandhiji said that it was a matter for shame that they had come to pray to God but failed to conduct the prayer peacefully.
('86', 139, 8, 18, 186205) People shouted and did not allow the prayer to go on, as it should go on.
('86', 139, 9, 19, 186279) Continuing, he said that he had been told by a friend that the people of Bombay would derive no benefit from his prayer.
('86', 139, 9, 20, 186400) They would throw a few rupees for the Harijan Fund, but if he thought that it was going to produce any effect on them or
('86', 139, 10, 21, 186521) 1 The meeting was attended by about 30,000 people.
('86', 139, 10, 22, 186572) Khan Abdul Ghaffar Khan was among those present.
('86', 139, 10, 23, 186621) 2 The crowd attending the prayer had become unmanageable at one stage and a number of people including Sushila Nayyar and Krishna Hatheesingh had got hurt in the rush.
('86', 140, 0, 1, 186789) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 141
('86', 140, 1, 2, 186830) that they would embrace the Harijans as their own kith and kin he was mistaken.
('86', 140, 2, 3, 186910) If you want, you go to Bombay.
('86', 140, 2, 4, 186941) You will get money but as far as prayers are concerned, it is better to stay at home and pray, the friend had warned him.
('86', 140, 3, 5, 187063) Gandhiji said that he was not entirely convinced.
('86', 140, 3, 6, 187113) They could not see God with the naked eye.
('86', 140, 3, 7, 187156) They could not touch Him with their hands.
('86', 140, 3, 8, 187199) He had become an untouchable.
('86', 140, 3, 9, 187229) And no wonder, considering that there was so much sin abroad, such violence, drinking and gambling.
('86', 140, 3, 10, 187329) Forty crores of people were in serfdom.
('86', 140, 3, 11, 187369) This was because they only talked of freedom but they did not know what freedom was really worth.
('86', 140, 3, 12, 187467) But he told this friend that he had always conducted prayers for a long time.
('86', 140, 3, 13, 187545) He was a firm believer in prayer.
('86', 140, 3, 14, 187579) Every religion had taught that man was no man if he did not pray to his Maker.
('86', 140, 3, 15, 187658) Therefore he had told this friend that though there was not much chance of his advice being followed, he could not give up his principles.
('86', 140, 3, 16, 187797) If he did not trust the people even that much, he would be worth nothing.
('86', 140, 3, 17, 187871) If he gave up prayer the next thing for him to do would be to give up the struggle for freedom, the striving for truth and non violence.
('86', 140, 4, 18, 188008) He told the people that they should let him come and go without rushing towards him.
('86', 140, 4, 19, 188093) They should keep silent during prayers.
('86', 140, 5, 20, 188133) In conclusion, Gandhiji asked them how, if they could not control themselves, they could wield the reins of power.
('86', 140, 5, 21, 188248) He would come there the next day and every day thereafter as long as he stayed in Bombay.
('86', 140, 5, 22, 188338) He would watch how far his words had gone home.
('86', 140, 5, 23, 188386) He would find out how far they were fit to govern themselves.
('86', 140, 5, 24, 188448) The man with God in his heart would know how to control himself.
('86', 140, 5, 25, 188513) The Bombay Chronicle, 4 4 1945
