('86', 146, 1, 2, 194765) 277. SPEECH AT PRAYER MEETING
('86', 146, 2, 3, 194795) BOMBAY April 6, 1945
('86', 146, 3, 4, 194816) Gandhiji began by asking people to keep silent and listen patiently to whatever he had to say.
('86', 146, 3, 5, 194911) Nobody should clap hands.
('86', 146, 3, 6, 194937) He wanted their ear; he wanted their heart.
('86', 146, 3, 7, 194981) If his words reached their hearts through their ears, he would be satisfied.
('86', 146, 4, 8, 195058) He congratulated them on their disciplined behaviour since Tuesday.
('86', 146, 4, 9, 195126) On that day two women had been hurt.
('86', 146, 4, 10, 195163) They had been perhaps touched by the incident and had decided to maintain discipline and allow the prayers to go on as usual.
('86', 146, 4, 11, 195289) On that day, there was a large crowd not lakhs but a few thousands.
('86', 146, 4, 12, 195357) Whether it was because of thefact that there were fewer people or for any other reason, he was glad to find that they had learnt discipline.
('86', 146, 4, 13, 195498) If they wanted to live together the first lesson they should learn was one of discipline.
('86', 146, 5, 14, 195588) Continuing, Gandhiji said that he was a Gujarati and should normally speak in Gujarati.
('86', 146, 5, 15, 195676) But it had been decided that whenever there was a cosmopolitan gathering they should speak in the national language.
('86', 146, 5, 16, 195793) He was responsible for that decision as much as others.
('86', 146, 5, 17, 195849) They had also to learn both the scripts, namely, Nagari and Urdu.
('86', 146, 5, 18, 195915) And they should learn to speak in such a simple way that everybody would understand it.
('86', 146, 5, 19, 196003) He had now realized that Urdu, Hindi, and Hindustani were all the same language.
('86', 146, 5, 20, 196084) If they learnt that language they could deal with members of any community and people from any part of India.
('86', 146, 5, 21, 196194) It served him when he went to the Punjab.
('86', 146, 5, 22, 196236) It would serve him if he were to go to Kashmirhe had not been there, but he had some Kashmiri friends Jawaharlal was one of them.
('86', 146, 5, 23, 196366) Gandhiji said that it was wrong to refer to a Muslim language or a Muslim script.
('86', 146, 5, 24, 196448) Both Hindus and Muslims wrote that language and if they wanted to steal the hearts of these people, they should be able to speak the same language and write in that script.
('86', 146, 6, 25, 196621) Adverting to the National Week, Gandhiji said that they had been observing the Week for the last 26 years.
('86', 146, 6, 26, 196728) Its observance was meant for the purification of their thoughts and their language.
('86', 146, 6, 27, 196812) In the beginning, the Week commenced with a fast.
('86', 146, 6, 28, 196862) He had since abandoned that.
('86', 146, 6, 29, 196891) He had also abandoned hartal.
('86', 146, 6, 30, 196921) The Week, however, had not become less holy on that account.
('86', 146, 6, 31, 196982) The fifteen point programme was there.
('86', 146, 6, 32, 197021) It began with khadi.
('86', 146, 6, 33, 197042) From that followed other items.
('86', 146, 6, 34, 197074) On such a holy day the people should begin to observe the fifteen point programme.
('86', 146, 6, 35, 197157) He was not asking them to observe it only for the Week but for all time.
('86', 146, 6, 36, 197230) They should not only follow it themselves but induce other people to do so.
('86', 146, 6, 37, 197306) If they wanted to make India free and not wait for others to free her, if they wanted to get freedom by truthful and non violent means, there was no other way.
('86', 146, 6, 38, 197466) But if it was to be by violence and revolution, that was another thing.
('86', 147, 0, 1, 197538) 148 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('86', 147, 1, 2, 197580) He had not known that method; he had not learnt it.
('86', 147, 1, 3, 197632) Freedom would not fall from the skies nor would it rise from the deep.
('86', 147, 1, 4, 197703) If they wanted to get it from their own efforts, there was only one way.
('86', 147, 2, 5, 197776) Some people thought in terms of Parliament.
('86', 147, 2, 6, 197820) He did not want to utter its name.
('86', 147, 2, 7, 197855) He wanted to forget Parliament but to think only of the constructive programme.
('86', 147, 2, 8, 197935) An important item of this programme was Hindu Muslim unity.
('86', 147, 3, 9, 197995) Concluding, Gandhiji said: Freedom is in our hands.
('86', 147, 3, 10, 198047) When we breathe, we cannot take other peoples help.
('86', 147, 3, 11, 198099) If we resort to artificial methods of respiration, it means that we are on the brink of death.
('86', 147, 3, 12, 198194) Freedom is like our breath.Having lost it for a long time we do appreciate it.
('86', 147, 3, 13, 198273) But I know the nature of freedom.
('86', 147, 3, 14, 198307) I have fully experienced freedom.
('86', 147, 3, 15, 198341) And if you regard it as holy and worthy of achievement, this is the only way.
('86', 147, 4, 16, 198419) The Bombay Chronicle, 7 4 1945

('86', 155, 6, 11, 207065) 295. INTERVIEW TO B. E. S. T. WORKERS DEPUTATION 1
('86', 155, 7, 12, 207116) BOMBAY, April 8, 1945 2
('86', 155, 8, 13, 207140) In reply to the request of the deputationists for advice Gandhiji said: My advice in this matter may not be of much use as, with the exception of Abidally, I am not acquainted with any of you.
('86', 155, 8, 14, 207333) Nor have I any direct, intimate knowledge of the conditions in Bombay.
('86', 155, 8, 15, 207404) 1 would therefore say to you that you should consult such leaders as enjoy your confidence and are sound and you should do as they say.
('86', 155, 9, 16, 207540) Pressed by the deputationists to give a word of guidance on the strength of his own experience of strikes which he had led, Gandhiji observed: I have conducted many strikes.
('86', 155, 9, 17, 207714) I can, therefore, give you the conditions of a successful strike.
('86', 155, 9, 18, 207780) The first is that the cause should be clear and just.
('86', 155, 9, 19, 207834) Secondly, the strikers should be firm and not be afraid of starvation, physical assaults or even death.
('86', 155, 9, 20, 207938) Thirdly, they should never deviate from the path of truth and ahimsa in whatever they
('86', 155, 10, 21, 208024) 1 The B.E.S.T. workers had been on strike and had sought Gandhijis advice.
('86', 155, 10, 22, 208099) As it was Gandhijis silence day he gave his remarks in writing.
('86', 155, 10, 23, 208163) The report given here was contained in a statement issued by Pyarelal in view of the fact that the Press had earlier published an unauthorized translation.
('86', 155, 10, 24, 208319) 2 From The Hindu, 10 4 1945
('86', 156, 0, 1, 208347) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 157
('86', 156, 1, 2, 208388) might do.
('86', 156, 1, 3, 208398) Fourthly, the strikers should have public support behind them.
('86', 156, 1, 4, 208461) If you can satisfy all these four conditions you should stand firm, but if you fall short in any of these respects you should boldly retrace your steps.
('86', 156, 1, 5, 208614) I cannot give you further guidance.
('86', 156, 1, 6, 208650) The details are for you to decide.
('86', 156, 2, 7, 208685) In answer to their further request that he should address an appeal to the Directors of the Company, most of whom were Indians, Gandhiji said: It is not my practice to interfere in a matter with which I am not fully acquainted.
('86', 156, 2, 8, 208913) I do not even know who are on the Board of Directors.
('86', 156, 2, 9, 208967) If, as you say, the Board is composed predominantly of Indians your task ought to be easy.
('86', 156, 2, 10, 209058) My function ceases with the advice.
('86', 156, 2, 11, 209094) The time is perhaps past when I could lead strikes myself.
('86', 156, 2, 12, 209153) If you understand this limitation of mine you will save my time as wellas yours.
('86', 156, 2, 13, 209234) Time in your case is the very essence.
('86', 156, 2, 14, 209273) You have therefore to act promptly.
('86', 156, 2, 15, 209309) If you carefully ponder over what I have said you will find that I have told you everything.
('86', 156, 3, 16, 209402) The deputationists finally asked whether Gandhiji would not appeal to the public to support them.
('86', 156, 3, 17, 209500) Gandhiji replied: It is not my word but your conduct that can win for you public support.
('86', 156, 3, 18, 209590) The Bombay Chronicle, 12 4 1945
('86', 156, 4, 19, 209622) 296. LETTER TO G. D. BIRLA
('86', 156, 5, 20, 209649) April 9, 1945
('86', 156, 6, 21, 209663) GHANSHYAMDAS, Can you read my handwriting?
('86', 156, 6, 22, 209706) If you find it difficult, I shall in future dictate my letters.
('86', 156, 6, 23, 209770) Days pass and there is no time left for a heart to heart talk.
('86', 156, 6, 24, 209833) I shall, therefore, put down in writing what I have to say.
('86', 156, 6, 25, 209893) That way I should be able to have my say.

('86', 160, 6, 12, 215383) 301. INTERVIEW TO K. R. NARAYANAN 1
('86', 160, 7, 13, 215419) April 10, 1945
('86', 160, 8, 14, 215434) Q. Do you still hold that the Harijan problem is only religious and social and that it has no great political significance?
('86', 160, 9, 15, 215558) A. It has political significance but indirectly.
('86', 160, 10, 16, 215607) Q. The Congress as an organization has not taken up the Harijan work.
('86', 160, 10, 17, 215677) Will it not be better if that work is taken up by the Congress and not by the Harijan Sevak Sangh?
('86', 160, 11, 18, 215776) A. It is wrong to say that the Congress has not taken it up.
('86', 160, 12, 19, 215837) Q. But it seems that leaders like Jawaharlal and the Rashtrapati are not keenly aware of the Harijan question?
('86', 160, 13, 20, 215948) A. Those two are immersed in that work.
('86', 160, 14, 21, 215988) Q. The Harijan Sevak Sangh after years of work had not yet produced even a dozen leaders from among the Harijans themselves.
('86', 160, 15, 22, 216113) A. That charge is only partly true.
('86', 160, 16, 23, 216149) Q. All great men have a passion for simplification.
('86', 160, 16, 24, 216201) You have simplified the

('86', 162, 1, 2, 217860) 303. SPEECH AT BORIVLI CAMP 1
('86', 162, 2, 3, 217890) April 11, 1945
('86', 162, 3, 4, 217905) Gandhiji began his remarks by requesting them 2 to give him a little respite.
('86', 162, 3, 5, 217983) There was a time and place for everything in life, he told them.
('86', 162, 3, 6, 218048) He had trained himself to listen to the inner voice irrespective of his surroundings.
('86', 162, 3, 7, 218134) But in that he had succeeded only partially.
('86', 162, 3, 8, 218179) He could not keep himself absolutely unaffected by his surroundings.
('86', 162, 3, 9, 218248) Therefore he requested the photographers to spare him while he was trying to express his deepest feelings.
('86', 162, 3, 10, 218355) Photography out of time and place was not art but vulgarity.
('86', 162, 4, 11, 218416) Dealing with the question of prayer he said that he had learnt that common prayers had been excluded from their routine lest anyone should feel that religion was being imposed upon her or him.
('86', 162, 4, 12, 218609) Speaking for himself he could say that he could do and had often done without food for days on end, but he could not do without prayer even for a single day.
('86', 162, 4, 13, 218767) Individual prayer was there but no one should fight shy of collective prayer.
('86', 162, 4, 14, 218845) Man is a social being.
('86', 162, 4, 15, 218868) If men and women could eat together, play together and work together why should they not pray together?
('86', 162, 4, 16, 218972) Why should anyone feel the need to pray away from everybodys gaze?
('86', 162, 4, 17, 219039) Was there anything sinful orshameful in prayer that it should not be said in public?
('86', 162, 4, 18, 219124) For close on fifty years he had been a believer in public prayer.
('86', 162, 4, 19, 219190) From his earliest days in South Africa he had among his associates and co workers men and women of every religion.
('86', 162, 4, 20, 219305) Hindus, Muslims, Christians and Parsis, all used to join him in prayer.
('86', 162, 4, 21, 219377) In India men and women in crowds attended his prayers wherever he went.
('86', 162, 4, 22, 219449) He had been told that they did not come to attend the prayers.
('86', 162, 4, 23, 219512) They came just to have his darshan.
('86', 162, 4, 24, 219548) Even if it was so, they came because they wanted to join him  a man of prayer.
('86', 162, 4, 25, 219627) He was aware that he had not come as near to God as he wanted to.
('86', 162, 4, 26, 219693) His realization of truth and ahimsa was still far from perfect, otherwise there would be no need for him to use speech.
('86', 162, 4, 27, 219813) His very being would radiate truth and ahimsa so that they would be able to see it on his face and feel its presence.
('86', 162, 4, 28, 219931) He had often said that the perfect ahimsa of one individual was quite enough for the whole world.
('86', 162, 4, 29, 220029) Whatever measure of success he had attained in the realization of truth and non violence was the result of prayer.
('86', 162, 5, 30, 220144) Prayer should be a spontaneous welling up of the heart.
('86', 162, 5, 31, 220200) One should not pray if one felt that prayer was a burden.
('86', 162, 5, 32, 220258) God was not hungry for mans prayer or praise.
('86', 162, 5, 33, 220304) He tolerated all because He was all Love.
('86', 162, 5, 34, 220346) If they felt that they owed a debt to Him who is the Giver of all things they should remember Him and pray to Him out of sheer
('86', 162, 6, 35, 220473) 1 The camp was organized by Mridula Sarabhai under the auspices of the Kasturba Gandhi National Memorial Fund.
('86', 162, 6, 36, 220584) 2 The cameramen who had been clicking continuously
('86', 163, 0, 1, 220635) 164 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('86', 163, 1, 2, 220677) gratitude.
('86', 163, 1, 3, 220688) The fear of incurring anybodys ridicule or displeasure should never deter one from performing ones elementary duty towards the Maker.
('86', 163, 1, 4, 220822) To illustrate his remark he told them the story of Prophet Daniel.
('86', 163, 2, 5, 220889) Answering next Shrimati Mridulabehns question as to what were the good and bad points of Indians as a nation, he observed that he was convinced that in the sum the former far outweighed the latter.
('86', 163, 2, 6, 221087) Indians had many defects.
('86', 163, 2, 7, 221113) India was a slave country and her slavery dated much farther back than the British conquest of India.
('86', 163, 2, 8, 221215) Slavery of evil customs and superstitions he knew, was the worst form of slavery.
('86', 163, 2, 9, 221297) Yet the solace that he could find in India he could find nowhere else.
('86', 163, 2, 10, 221368) He had lived in England and he had spent the best part of his life in South Africa.
('86', 163, 2, 11, 221452) Yet he could not adopt those countries as his home.
('86', 163, 2, 12, 221504) In reply to a friends query years ago he had said that he wanted to die in the lap of his mother.
('86', 163, 2, 13, 221602) His own mother, who was a frail little woman, had died years ago.
('86', 163, 2, 14, 221668) But Mother India with her 80 crores of hands 80 crores of feet and 40 crores of mouths had beckoned to him from across the seas and he could not resist that call.
('86', 163, 3, 15, 221831) What did it matter if that venerable mother appeared sick and paralysed today?
('86', 163, 3, 16, 221910) It was not for him to proclaim Indias virtues.
('86', 163, 3, 17, 221957) As for her shortcomings he had been proclaiming them from the house tops ever since his return to India.
('86', 163, 3, 18, 222062) But if he were pressed to name only one shortcoming of Indians he would say that the worst was cowardice.
('86', 163, 4, 19, 222168) Another friend asked how women could go into the villages and work under the Kasturba Gandhi National Memorial Fund scheme handicapped as they wereby so many restrictions.
('86', 163, 4, 20, 222340) Gandhijis reply was that he had expected that their first lesson in the camp was to learn to break all social restrictions that cramped or degraded them.
('86', 163, 4, 21, 222494) He, however, warned them that this did not mean throwing off of all moral restraints.
('86', 163, 4, 22, 222580) There was at present a woeful deterioration of moral standards in society among men.
('86', 163, 4, 23, 222665) Even those who talked loudly about enforcing monogamy through law did not practise it themselves.
('86', 163, 4, 24, 222763) The same tendency was beginning to manifest itself among women.
('86', 163, 4, 25, 222827) He had known educated girls who thought nothing of marrying men having a living wife.
('86', 163, 4, 26, 222913) He called this degradation of womanhood.
('86', 163, 4, 27, 222954) Such views could not be defended under the pretence of banishing social superstitions or vice.
('86', 163, 4, 28, 223049) Did the emancipation of women mean that they should imitate men in that respect?
('86', 163, 4, 29, 223130) Certainly not.
('86', 163, 4, 30, 223145) India could never win swaraj, certainly not the swaraj of his conception, by following that path.
('86', 163, 5, 31, 223243) Uttermost moral purity was the first requisite for establishing social freedom.
('86', 163, 5, 32, 223323) No one who lacked moral purity was qualified to lead a crusade against evil social restrictions.
('86', 163, 6, 33, 223420) The next question was how they were to deal with the question of untouchability in the villages.
('86', 163, 6, 34, 223517) He agreed that the problem of untouchability in the
('86', 164, 0, 1, 223569) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 165
('86', 164, 1, 2, 223610) villages was very acute.
('86', 164, 1, 3, 223635) But those who went there should go with the grim determination to destroy it root and branch or perish in the attempt.
('86', 164, 1, 4, 223754) They should begin with the scavengers.
('86', 164, 1, 5, 223793) Unfortunately, there was untouchability even among the so called untouchables.
('86', 164, 1, 6, 223872) They should mix with them and eat and drink with them, provided they observed the rules of cleanliness and sanitation.
('86', 164, 1, 7, 223991) They could inculcate these habits upon them by cooking for them and cleaning up their homes for them.
('86', 164, 2, 8, 224093) Another question expressed the fear that since capitalists had contributed the bulk of the Kasturba Gandhi National Memorial Fund and since they were taken on committees their influence would dominate the organization and vitiate it.
('86', 164, 3, 9, 224327) Gandhiji dismissed the apprehension as groundless.
('86', 164, 3, 10, 224378) He maintained that in endorsing the acceptance of donations of the rich he had not in any way accepted their dictation nor did they seek or expect any such thing from him.
('86', 164, 3, 11, 224550) Moneyed men were in a majority only in the Board of Trustees, but that did not mean that they dominated or wanted to dominate the organization.
('86', 164, 3, 12, 224694) In fact they had offered voluntarily to retire from the Board after the fund had been collected and would have gladly done so had he expressed such a desire.
('86', 164, 3, 13, 224852) But he wanted not only their donations but their talent goodwill and services for the cause and so they continued to be on the Board.
('86', 164, 4, 14, 224986) He refused to believe that the capitalists were necessarily a bad lot or worse than members of any other class.
('86', 164, 4, 15, 225098) In this world everyone was imperfect.
('86', 164, 4, 16, 225136) He was too well aware of his own imperfections to presume to judge others.
('86', 164, 4, 17, 225211) His ahimsa required him to be rigorous in viewing his own shortcomings but to be charitable in judging others.
('86', 164, 4, 18, 225322) It was enough if he could eradicate his own.
('86', 164, 4, 19, 225367) If, therefore, instead of cavillingat the faults of others we turned the searchlight inward and concentrated on self purification, the world would become a better place to live in and the general social purification would be reflected in the capitalist class too.
('86', 164, 4, 20, 225631) He could not therefore say to the capitalists that unless they renounced all their riches he would have nothing to do with them.
('86', 164, 4, 21, 225760) Complete renunciation of ones possessions was a thing which very few even among the ordinary folk were capable of.
('86', 164, 4, 22, 225875) All that one could legitimately expect of the wealthy class was to hold their riches in trust and use them for the service of society.
('86', 164, 4, 23, 226010) To insist upon more would be to kill the goose that laid the golden eggs.
('86', 164, 4, 24, 226084) The Bombay Chronicle, 13 4 1945
('86', 165, 0, 1, 226116) 166 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('86', 165, 1, 2, 226158) 304. SPEECH AT PRAYER MEETING
('86', 165, 2, 3, 226188) BORIVLI, April 11, 1945
('86', 165, 3, 4, 226212) Gandhiji said he was reminded by Balasaheb Kher that he had visited Borivli after twenty years.
('86', 165, 3, 5, 226308) He did not think it was such a long time.
('86', 165, 3, 6, 226350) He was glad to be able to renew their acquaintance after such a long period.
('86', 165, 3, 7, 226427) On them rested a great responsibility owing to Shrimati Mridulabehns shibir in their midst.
('86', 165, 3, 8, 226519) They should interest themselves in it.
('86', 165, 3, 9, 226558) He then turned to Khan Saheb and said, if he was to be friends with Khan Saheb was he to expect him to learn Sanskritized Hindi or was he, the speaker, bound to speak and write to him in Urdu?
('86', 165, 3, 10, 226751) But Khan Saheb was everyones friend.
('86', 165, 3, 11, 226788) Therefore it was the duty of the audience to learn the national language in both the forms and both scripts.
('86', 165, 3, 12, 226897) Thus and thus alone could the All India language permeate the whole of India.
('86', 165, 3, 13, 226975) In this at least there should be no Pakistan and he who wished to make common cause with Hindus and Muslims was bound to learn the two scripts and two forms.
('86', 165, 3, 14, 227133) A time would then come when the two forms of speech would become one.
('86', 165, 3, 15, 227203) If they felt it a burden to learn the scripts, he could only say swaraj was not to be had easily and without toil.
('86', 165, 3, 16, 227318) Where there was love toil was no trouble but pleasure.
('86', 165, 4, 17, 227373) The speaker then alluded to the evening bhajan sung at the prayer.
('86', 165, 4, 18, 227440) Its burden was that the way to God was for the valiant, not for the timid.
('86', 165, 4, 19, 227515) But God was not to be reached by slaves.
('86', 165, 4, 20, 227556) Therefore the bhajan was also for those who wanted to throw off their slavery.
('86', 165, 5, 21, 227635) The speaker then concluded that slavery must be the lot of those who hugged untouchability and that too in the name of religion.
('86', 165, 5, 22, 227764) He wanted therefore to repeat what he had said so often, namely, that Hinduism must perish if untouchability lived.

('86', 166, 1, 2, 228026) 305. LETTER TO M. S. KELKAR
('86', 166, 2, 3, 228054) BOMBAY, April 12, 1945
('86', 166, 3, 4, 228077) MY DEAR ICE, You are right.
('86', 166, 3, 5, 228105) It is perhaps shameful on my part to exile myself for three months for coolness sake.

('86', 168, 5, 13, 231182) 310. NOTE TO SARALADEVI SARABHAI
('86', 168, 6, 14, 231215) April 12, 1945 I have no difficulty in agreeing with the scientific views of Madame Montessori.
('86', 168, 6, 15, 231311) However, if they are propagated in their Western garb in Indian villages they are more likely to prove useless and might even prove harmful, because in that garb they will be too expensive for Indian villages and ill adapted to the village atmosphere.
('86', 168, 6, 16, 231563) It is possible the cities may not feel the expense so much and women influenced by Western ways may be receptive to the ideas presented in Western garb; but even so it will be of no use because India lives not in cities but in its seven lakh villages.
('86', 168, 6, 17, 231815) Besides, scientific education with Western trappings might prove poisonous to the city dwellers because here education begins the moment the child is conceived and ends no one knows when.
('86', 168, 6, 18, 232003) These days the cities are created by the foreigners toserve their ends and so they do not represent the villages.
('86', 168, 6, 19, 232117) They do not protect the interests of the villagers but are becoming their exploiters.
('86', 168, 7, 20, 232203) SARALADEVI SARABHAI THE RETREAT SHAHIBAGH AHMEDABAD From a copy of the Gujarati: Pyarelal Papers.
('86', 168, 7, 21, 232301) Courtesy: Pyarelal

('86', 175, 1, 2, 238918) 323. A NOTE
('86', 175, 2, 3, 238930) April 15, 1945 I am sorry to say that what appears to have been meant as a supplement to the constructive programme is its flat contradiction.
('86', 175, 2, 4, 239073) And it is unworkable.
('86', 175, 2, 5, 239095) If put in action, it will [not only] frustrate itself but will largely hamper the constructive programme.
('86', 175, 2, 6, 239201) But this is merely a caution.
('86', 175, 2, 7, 239231) Those who believe in this programme must prosecute it till they are convinced to the contrary.
('86', 175, 2, 8, 239326) That is the best argument.
('86', 175, 2, 9, 239353) Hence I do not want to reason even if I had the time which I have not just now.
('86', 175, 4, 10, 239433) From a copy: Jawaharlal Nehru Papers, Part: Vol. IV.
('86', 175, 4, 11, 239486) Courtesy: Nehru Memorial Museum and Library

('86', 177, 6, 11, 241541) 328. FRAGMENT OF LETTER TO SHARAYU DHOTRE 3
('86', 177, 7, 12, 241585) April 15, 1945 In my view the question is not difficult.
('86', 177, 7, 13, 241642) I shall define the ideal.
('86', 177, 7, 14, 241668) It is for each individual to decide how far it is proper to depart from it.
('86', 177, 7, 15, 241744) Consider also that my own conduct is not in keeping with the ideal I lay down.
('86', 177, 7, 16, 241823) My coming here and then going to Mahabaleshwar is a breach of the ideal.
('86', 177, 7, 17, 241896) Even so, that is what I am doing.
('86', 177, 7, 18, 241930) You are similarly free to act as you wish.
('86', 177, 7, 19, 241973) If the heart is inclined in a certain way the ideal is secondary.
('86', 177, 7, 20, 242039) Let us do without what everyone cannot have.
('86', 177, 7, 21, 242084) I have told you that in practice we do not do it.
('86', 177, 7, 22, 242134) Now you have to decide without hesitation whether or not you should take help from Saroj or Raihana or Kamalnayan.
('86', 177, 7, 23, 242249) Neither I nor anybody else should take that decision.
('86', 177, 8, 24, 242303) Blessings from BAPU
('86', 177, 9, 25, 242323) From Hindi: C.W. 841. Courtesy: Sharayu Dhotre

('86', 180, 1, 2, 244880) 333. SPEECH AT PRAYER MEETING
('86', 180, 2, 3, 244910) BOMBAY, April 15, 1945
('86', 180, 3, 4, 244933) Gandhiji wanted to refer to a conversation he had with a friend.
('86', 180, 3, 5, 244998) He was asked to define who was a Gandhi ite as there was confusion in the public mind.
('86', 180, 3, 6, 245085) He could safely say there was no Gandhi ite in India.
('86', 180, 3, 7, 245139) He was himself not one.
('86', 180, 3, 8, 245163) He had founded no cult.
('86', 180, 3, 9, 245187) He claimed to be a satyagrahi and therefore, he was also non violent, or was trying to be and he invited everyone in the audience to do likewise.
('86', 180, 4, 10, 245333) When the odds were heavy against them in South Africa, where they were in a hopeless minority, he had discovered satyagraha in 1906 in the place of parliamentary programme.
('86', 180, 4, 11, 245506) He had never been a member of any parliament or even a local board.
('86', 180, 4, 12, 245574) He saw that non violent non co operation was the most powerful thing instead.
('86', 180, 4, 13, 245652) The constructive part was his 15 point programme which they had seen.
('86', 180, 4, 14, 245722) There was swaraj in it and much more.
('86', 180, 5, 15, 245760) Satyagraha was not a mere policy with him, it was his creed.
('86', 180, 5, 16, 245821) He hoped to see God face to face through it.
('86', 180, 5, 17, 245866) If that was the power of satyagraha surely political swaraj was a simple matter if all took to it.
('86', 180, 6, 18, 245965) But his satyagraha told him that he was to bear with those who did not see eye to eye with him but sought to go through the parliamentary programme.
('86', 180, 6, 19, 246114) They had known him closeted with Dr. Khan Saheb and his friends as also with Advocate Bhulabhai Desai.
('86', 180, 6, 20, 246217) He told them to follow their belief.
('86', 180, 6, 21, 246254) He owned no enemycertainly not Englishmen and not even English officials.
('86', 180, 6, 22, 246328) But that did not mean that he should follow them.
('86', 180, 6, 23, 246378) He went his own way.
('86', 180, 6, 24, 246399) The official way was to rule India, his was to serve India.
('86', 180, 6, 25, 246459) The official was all for power, he was all for service and that in the name of God.
('86', 180, 6, 26, 246543) Therefore he could afford to face the whole worlds opposition, for God, he believed, was with him and He was a never failing, all sufficing companion and infallible Guide.
('86', 180, 6, 27, 246715) The Bombay Chronicle, 16 4 1945
('86', 181, 0, 1, 246747) 182 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('86', 181, 1, 2, 246789) 334. ANSWERS TO QUESTIONS 1
('86', 181, 2, 3, 246817) [April 16, 1945] 2
('86', 181, 3, 4, 246836) Instead of undertaking the thankless task of going through the jumble of my writings to find out what I have said or have not said about caste, you have done well in sending me the following questions.
('86', 181, 4, 5, 247038) 1. Do you still adhere to the views you have expressed on the caste system in your writings?
('86', 181, 5, 6, 247131) 2. Do you still believe that the caste system is the best social order and that the world should adopt it?
('86', 181, 6, 7, 247238) 3. Do you still believe that the thousands of existing sub castes will disappear and merge so that in the end only the four varnas will remain?
('86', 181, 6, 8, 247382) In the last twenty five years how many sub castes have thus disappeared and merged into bigger castes?
('86', 181, 7, 9, 247485) 4. Whatever castes we find in history are all based on birth and the inequalities arising therefrom.
('86', 181, 7, 10, 247586) Do you think that the equality and brotherhood you preach is consistent with that kind of social order?
('86', 181, 7, 11, 247690) If the Bhangis go on doing the work of scavenging from one generation to the next, what will be their future?
('86', 181, 8, 12, 247800) 5. Isnt Shri Sanjanas severe criticism of the Politics of the Cow entirely true?
('86', 181, 9, 13, 247881) 6. Will you give your consent to the bill introduced in the Central Legislature for retaining caste differences in the Hindu Law?
('86', 181, 10, 14, 248011) 7. The Congress is an orthodox Hindu organization and under the fostering care of Gandhiji it has become a missionary organization for the renewal and well being of the orthodox Hindu religion with its caste system. What reply would you give to such allegations of Shri Sanjana?
('86', 181, 10, 15, 248290) And if what Shri Sanjana says is correct, does it not repudiate the Congress claim of being a truly national organization?
('86', 181, 11, 16, 248413) 8. Is the caste system consistent with democracy and democratic organizations?
('86', 181, 11, 17, 248492) I do not need to refer to my past writings to say what I believe
('86', 181, 12, 18, 248557) 1 The questions had been submitted to Gandhiji by a correspondent and included quotations from Gandhijis writings.
('86', 181, 12, 19, 248672) Gandhiji, in answering, summarized these.
('86', 181, 12, 20, 248714) Later the questions and the answers were published by Navajivan as a preface to Varnavyavastha.
('86', 181, 12, 21, 248810) These were also published in The Bombay Chronicle and The Hindu.
('86', 181, 12, 22, 248875) 2 From The Bombay Chronicle, 17 4 1945
('86', 182, 0, 1, 248914) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 183
('86', 182, 1, 2, 248955) today, because only what I believe today counts.
('86', 182, 1, 3, 249004) I wish to say that the caste system as it exists to day in Hinduism is an anachronism.
('86', 182, 1, 4, 249091) It is one of those ugly things which will certainly hinder the growth of true religion.
('86', 182, 1, 5, 249179) It must go if both Hinduism and India are to live and grow from day today.
('86', 182, 1, 6, 249254) The way to do it is for all Hindus to become their own scavengers and treat the so called hereditary Bhangis as their own brothers.
('86', 182, 1, 7, 249386) I say the Bhangis because they are at the lowest rung of the ladder.
('86', 182, 1, 8, 249455) This answers all the questions and I need say nothing more.
('86', 182, 1, 9, 249515) It is evident that the questioner has not taken the trouble to read my writings.
('86', 182, 1, 10, 249596) 1 Everybody knows that the Congress from its inception has not been and is not even now an orthodox Hindu organization.
('86', 182, 1, 11, 249716) It is a democratic organization comprising people holding different views and is daily becoming more and more so under my fostering care.
('86', 182, 1, 12, 249854) MOHANDAS KARAMCHAND GANDHI [From Gujarati]
('86', 182, 2, 13, 249897) Varnavyavastha, pp.

('86', 187, 6, 11, 254754) 345. STATEMENT TO THE PRESS
('86', 187, 7, 12, 254782) BOMBAY, April 17, 1945 Though I know that silence is better than the spoken or written word, there are well defined limitations to the application of the maxim.
('86', 187, 7, 13, 254943) The San Francisco Conference is announced to meet shortly.
('86', 187, 8, 14, 255002) I do not know its agenda.
('86', 187, 8, 15, 255028) Probably no outsider knows it.
('86', 187, 8, 16, 255059) Whatever it may be, the Conference will have much to do with the world to be after the so called end of the war.
('86', 187, 8, 17, 255172) I very much fear that behind the structure of world security sought to be raised lurk mistrust and fear which breed war.
('86', 187, 8, 18, 255293) Therefore as a lifelong believer in peace as against war, it seems well for me to record my convictions in the matter.
('86', 187, 8, 19, 255412) I reiterate my conviction that there will be no peace for the Allies or the world unless they shed their belief in the efficacy of war and its accompanying terrible deception and fraud and are determined to hammer out real peace based on freedom and equality of all races and nations.
('86', 187, 8, 20, 255697) Exploitation and domination of one nationover another can have no place in a world striving to put an end
('86', 187, 9, 21, 255803) 1 The Conference was convened on April 25 and concluded on June 26 when the Charter of the United Nations was finally adopted.
('86', 188, 0, 1, 255930) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 189
('86', 188, 1, 2, 255971) to all wars.
('86', 188, 1, 3, 255984) It is only in such a world that the militarily weaker nations will be free from the fear of intimidation or exploitation.
('86', 188, 1, 4, 256106) (1) An indispensable preliminary to peace is the complete freedom of India from all foreign control, not merely because it is a classic example of imperialist domination but specially because it is a big, ancient and cultured country which has fought for its freedom since 1920 deliberately with Truth and Nonviolence as its only weapon.
('86', 188, 1, 5, 256444) Though the Indian soldier has fought not for Indias freedom, he has shown during this war as never before that he is at least an equal of the best in his fighting qualities.
('86', 188, 1, 6, 256618) I cite this to answer the charge that Indias peaceful struggle is due to its lack of soldierly quality.
('86', 188, 1, 7, 256722) The inevitable deduction that is drawn from this is that non violence of the strong is infinitely braver than their violence.
('86', 188, 1, 8, 256848) That India may not yet have evolved such non violence is another matter.
('86', 188, 1, 9, 256921) If it is the case, it does not detract from the statement that it has battled non violently for freedom and that not without considerable success.
('86', 188, 1, 10, 257068) (2) Freedom of India will demonstrate to all the exploited races of the earth that their freedom is very near and that in no case will they henceforth be exploited.
('86', 188, 1, 11, 257233) (3) Peace must be just.
('86', 188, 1, 12, 257257) In order to be that, it must neither be punitive nor vindictive.
('86', 188, 1, 13, 257322) Germany and Japan should not be humiliated.
('86', 188, 1, 14, 257366) The strong are never vindictive.
('86', 188, 1, 15, 257399) Therefore, fruits of peace must be equally shared.
('86', 188, 1, 16, 257450) The effort then will be to turn them into friends.
('86', 188, 1, 17, 257501) The Allies can prove their democracy by no other means.
('86', 188, 1, 18, 257557) (4) It follows from the foregoing that there will be no armed peace imposed upon the forcibly disarmed.
('86', 188, 1, 19, 257661) All will be disarmed.
('86', 188, 1, 20, 257683) There will be an international police force to enforce the lightest terms of peace.
('86', 188, 1, 21, 257767) Even this retention of an international police will be a concession to human weakness, not by any means an emblem of peace If these foregoing essentials of peace are accepted, it follows that the camouflage of Indian representation through Indians nominated by British imperialism should be dropped.
('86', 188, 1, 22, 258067) 1 Such representation will be worse than no representation.
('86', 188, 1, 23, 258127) Either India at SanFrancisco is represented by an elected representative or represented not at all.
('86', 188, 2, 24, 258227) 1 The British Government had nominated A. Ramaswamy Mudaliar, Firoz Khan Noon and V. T. Krishnamachari to represent India at the Conference.
('86', 189, 0, 1, 258368) 190 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('86', 189, 1, 2, 258410) The following from the Congress resolution of August 8, 1942, shows clearly what free India stands for:
('86', 189, 2, 3, 258514) While the A.I.C.C. must primarily be concerned with the independence and defence of India in this hour of danger, the Committee is of opinion that the future peace, security and ordered progress of the world demand a world federation of free nations, and on no other basis can the problems of the modern world be solved.
('86', 189, 2, 4, 258835) Such a world federation would ensure the freedom of its constituent nations, the prevention of aggression and exploitation by one nation over another, the protection of national minorities, the advancement of all backward areas and peoples, and the pooling of the worlds resources for the common good of all.
('86', 189, 2, 5, 259144) On the establishment of such a world federation, disarmament would be practicable in all countries, national armies, navies and air forces would no longer be necessary, and a world federal defence force would keep the world peace and prevent aggression.
('86', 189, 2, 6, 259398) An independent India would gladly join such a world federation and co operate on an equal basis with other countries in the solution of international problems.
('86', 189, 2, 7, 259558) Thus the demand for Indian independence is in no way selfish.
('86', 189, 2, 8, 259620) Its nationalism spells internationalism.
('86', 189, 2, 9, 259661) The Bombay Chronicle, 18 4 1945
('86', 189, 3, 10, 259693) 346. MESSAGE TO INDIANS IN SOUTH AFRICA 1
('86', 189, 4, 11, 259735) BOMBAY, April 18, 1945 As India holds the key to the freedom of all the exploited races and nations of the earth so do Indians in South Africa hold the key to the protection and freedom of the exploited people in the overseas.
('86', 189, 4, 12, 259962) For it was in South Africa that satyagraha was fairly tried and became largely successful.
('86', 189, 4, 13, 260053) Will the Indians there unite and sacrifice themselves for the common cause?
('86', 189, 5, 14, 260129) M. K. GANDHI

('86', 195, 8, 31, 268527) I am very keen to have yourwhole hearted support because you are you and I have a great respect for you.

('86', 198, 1, 2, 270854) 361. SPEECH AT PRAYER MEETING
('86', 198, 2, 3, 270884) BOMBAY, April 19, 1945
('86', 198, 3, 4, 270907) Gandhiji spoke of the value of prayer and asked the audience to continue the habit even after he was gone.
('86', 198, 3, 5, 271014) In particular he asked them to pray that the taint of untouchability might be removed root and branch and find no place in their hearts.
('86', 198, 4, 6, 271151) But he reminded them also that it was not enough if they prayed.
('86', 198, 4, 7, 271216) While everything ultimately depended on the will of God they must do their duty.
('86', 198, 4, 8, 271297) In the 15 point constructive programme which he had set out before them was hidden the key to swaraj.
('86', 198, 4, 9, 271399) If a large majority of them pursued this programme sincerely he was confident that their efforts would be crowned with success.
('86', 198, 5, 10, 271527) The Bombay Chronicle, 20 4 1945

('86', 206, 7, 17, 280739) MAHABALESHWAR, April 21, 1945
('86', 206, 8, 18, 280769) Mahatma Gandhi, addressing the gathering at the end of prayers, asked them to leave him alone to have peace.

('86', 206, 9, 21, 281099) Announcing that henceforth prayers would be held earlier in the day for the benefit of those who came from a distance, he said that those who attended prayers should come with a desire to participate in the prayers and not merely to have a look at him.

('86', 221, 1, 2, 297104) 408. LETTER TO GHANSHYAM MIRCHANDANI
('86', 221, 2, 3, 297141) MAHABALESHWAR, [Before April 25, 1945] 1
('86', 221, 3, 4, 297182) In your place I would not submit even if I were to die.
('86', 221, 3, 5, 297238) 2 But there is no one law for everyone.
('86', 221, 3, 6, 297278) You should act solely according to your capacity.
('86', 221, 3, 7, 297328) In any event seeing that you did not accept the notice, you should inform the authorities that you would not accept restrictions save of your own conscience and that you fully believed in non violence and truth.
('86', 221, 3, 8, 297540) The Bombay Chronicle, 26 4 1945
('86', 221, 4, 9, 297572) 409. INTERVIEW TO RALPH CONISTON 3
('86', 221, 5, 10, 297607) [Before April 25, 1945] 4
('86', 221, 6, 11, 297633) RALPH CONISTON: Why do you feel so sceptical about the possibility of a lasting peace emerging from the defeat of the Axis Powers?
('86', 221, 7, 12, 297764) GANDHIJI: The reason is patent.
('86', 221, 7, 13, 297796) Violence is bound sooner or later to exhaust itself but peace cannot issue out of such exhaustion.
('86', 221, 7, 14, 297895) I am uttering Gods truth when I say that unless there is a return to sanity, violent people will be swept off the face of the earth .
('86', 221, 7, 15, 298029) Those who have their hands dyed deep in blood cannot build a non violent order for the world.
('86', 221, 8, 16, 298123) R. C. While the representatives of the big powers who would be meeting at San Francisco were what they were, the people at large, after the experience of the horrors of war, would force the hands of their respective Governments.
('86', 221, 9, 17, 298352) G. I know the European mind well enough to know that when it has to choose between abstract justice and self interest, it will plump for the latter.
('86', 221, 9, 18, 298501) The man in the street even in America does not think much for himself.
('86', 221, 9, 19, 298572) He will put faith in what Roosevelt says.
('86', 221, 9, 20, 298614) Rooseveltgives him market, credit and all that.
('86', 221, 9, 21, 298662) Similarly Churchill can say to the English working class that he has kept the Empire intact and
('86', 221, 10, 22, 298758) 1 The news item carrying the letter is dated Karachi, April 25. 2 The addressee had sought Gandhijis advice in regard to the restraint order served upon him by the Sind Government.
('86', 221, 10, 23, 298939) 3 Of the Colliers Weekly 4 From the contents it is obvious that this discussion took place before the San Francisco Conference which opened on April 25, 1945.
('86', 222, 0, 1, 299098) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 223
('86', 222, 1, 2, 299139) preserved for them the foreign markets.
('86', 222, 1, 3, 299179) The people will, as they do, follow him.
('86', 222, 2, 4, 299220) R. C. So, you dont think that the average man in Europe or America cares much for the high ideals for which the war is professed to be fought?
('86', 222, 3, 5, 299363) G. I am afraid, I do not.
('86', 222, 3, 6, 299389) If you hold the contrary view, I shall honour you for your belief but I cannot share it.
('86', 222, 4, 7, 299478) R. C. Then, you dont think the Big Five or the Big Three can guarantee peace?
('86', 222, 5, 8, 299556) G. I am positive.
('86', 222, 5, 9, 299574) If they are so arrogant as to think that they can have lasting peace while the exploitation of the coloured and the so called backward races goes on, they are living in a fools paradise.
('86', 222, 6, 10, 299761) R. C. You think they will fall out among themselves before long?
('86', 222, 7, 11, 299826) G. There you are stealing my language.
('86', 222, 7, 12, 299865) The quarrel with Russia has already started.
('86', 222, 7, 13, 299910) It is only a question when the other twoEngland and Americawill start quarreling with each other.
('86', 222, 7, 14, 300008) Maybe, pure self interest will dictate a wiser course and those who will be meeting at San Francisco will say: Let us not fall out over a fallen carcass. The man in the street will gain nothing by it.
('86', 222, 7, 15, 300209) Freedom of India along non violent lines, on the other hand, will mean the biggest thing for the exploited races of the earth.
('86', 222, 7, 16, 300336) I am, therefore, trying to concentrate on it.
('86', 222, 7, 17, 300382) If India acts on the square when her turn comes, it will not dictate terms at the Peace Conference but peace and freedom will descend upon it, not as a terrifying torrent, but as gentle rain from heaven.
('86', 222, 7, 18, 300586) Liberty won non violently will belong to the least.
('86', 222, 7, 19, 300638) That is why I swear by non violence.
('86', 222, 7, 20, 300675) Only when the least can say, I have got my liberty have I got mine.
('86', 222, 8, 21, 300743) The conversation then turned on the issue of the treatment of the aggressor nations after the war.
('86', 222, 9, 22, 300842) G. As a non violent man, I do not believe in the punishment of individuals, much less can I stomach the punishment of a whole nation.
('86', 222, 10, 23, 300976) R. C. What about the war criminals?
('86', 222, 11, 24, 301012) G. What is a war criminal?
('86', 222, 11, 25, 301039) Was not war itself a crime against God and humanity and, therefore, were not all those who sanctioned, engineered, and conducted wars, war criminals?
('86', 222, 11, 26, 301189) War criminals are notconfined to the Axis Powers alone.
('86', 222, 11, 27, 301245) Roosevelt and Churchill are no less war criminals than Hitler and Mussolini.
('86', 222, 11, 28, 301322) Hitler was Great Britains sin.
('86', 222, 11, 29, 301353) Hitler is only an answer to British imperialism, and this I say in spite of the fact that I hate
('86', 223, 0, 1, 301450) 224 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('86', 223, 1, 2, 301492) Hitlerism and its anti Semitism.
('86', 223, 1, 3, 301525) England, America and Russia have all of them got their hands dyed more or less rednot merely Germany and Japan.
('86', 223, 1, 4, 301637) The Japanese have only proved themselves to be apt pupils of the West.
('86', 223, 1, 5, 301708) They have learnt at the feet of the West and beaten it at its own game.
('86', 223, 2, 6, 301780) R. C. What would you see accomplished at San Francisco?
('86', 223, 3, 7, 301836) G. Parity among all nationsthe strongest and the weakest the strong should be the servants of the weak not their masters or exploiters.
('86', 223, 4, 8, 301972) R. C. Is not this too idealistic?
('86', 223, 4, 9, 302006) But you asked me what I would like to see accomplished.
('86', 223, 4, 10, 302062) It is my belief that human nature is ever working upward.
('86', 223, 4, 11, 302120) I can, therefore, never take a pessimistic view of the future of human nature.
('86', 223, 4, 12, 302199) If the Big Five say, We shall hold on to what we have, the result will be a terrible catastrophe and then Heaven help the world and the Big Five.
('86', 223, 4, 13, 302345) There will be another and bloodier war and another San Francisco.
('86', 223, 5, 14, 302411) R. C. Would the results of the second San Francisco be any better than that of the first?
('86', 223, 6, 15, 302501) G. I hope so.
('86', 223, 6, 16, 302515) They will be saner then.
('86', 223, 6, 17, 302540) They will have gained their balance somewhat after their third experience.
('86', 223, 7, 18, 302615) R. C. Would you not go to the West to teach them the art of peace?
('86', 223, 8, 19, 302682) G. In the second World War some British pacifists, including Dick Sheppard and Maude Royden had written to me asking me to point the way.
('86', 223, 8, 20, 302820) My reply in substance was: Even if one of you can become true in the right sense of the word, that one man will be able to inculcate non violence among the European folk.
('86', 223, 8, 21, 302991) I cannot today save Europe, however much I may like to.
('86', 223, 8, 22, 303047) I know Europe and America.
('86', 223, 8, 23, 303074) If I go there I shall be like a stranger.
('86', 223, 8, 24, 303116) Probably I shall be lionized but that is all.
('86', 223, 8, 25, 303162) I shall not be able to present to them the science of peace in language they can understand.
('86', 223, 8, 26, 303255) But they will understand if I can make good my non violence in India.
('86', 223, 8, 27, 303325) I shall then speak through India.
('86', 223, 8, 28, 303359) I, therefore, declined to accept the invitations from America and Europe.
('86', 223, 8, 29, 303433) My answer would be the same today.
('86', 223, 9, 30, 303468) R. C. If you were at San Francisco, what would you be advocat ing there?
('86', 223, 10, 31, 303541) G. If I knew I would tell you but I am made differently.
('86', 223, 10, 32, 303598) When I face a situation, the solution comes to me.
('86', 223, 10, 33, 303649) I am not a man who sits down and thinks out problems syllogistically.
('86', 223, 10, 34, 303719) I am a man of action.
('86', 224, 0, 1, 303741) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 225
('86', 224, 1, 2, 303782) react to a situation intuitively.
('86', 224, 1, 3, 303816) Logic comes afterwards, it does not precede the event.
('86', 224, 1, 4, 303871) The moment I am at the Peace Conference, I know the right word will come.
('86', 224, 1, 5, 303945) But not beforehand.
('86', 224, 1, 6, 303965) This much, however, I can say that whatever I say there will be in terms of peace, not war.
('86', 224, 2, 7, 304057) R. C. What kind of world organization would promote an enduring peace or preserve it?
('86', 224, 3, 8, 304143) G. Only an organization based predominantly on truth and non violence.
('86', 224, 4, 9, 304214) R. C. With the present imperfect condition of the world and human nature, what means would in your opinion promote peace?
('86', 224, 5, 10, 304336) G. Nearest approach to the condition laid down in my answer to the previous question.
('86', 224, 6, 11, 304422) R. C. Would you have a world government?
('86', 224, 7, 12, 304463) G. Yes.
('86', 224, 7, 13, 304471) I claim to be a practical idealist.
('86', 224, 7, 14, 304507) I believe in compromise so long as it does not involve the sacrifice of principles.
('86', 224, 7, 15, 304591) I may not get a world government that I want just now but if it is a government that would just touch my ideal, I would accept it as a compromise.
('86', 224, 7, 16, 304738) Therefore, although I am not enamoured of a world federation, I shall be prepared to accept it if it is built on an essentially non violent basis.
('86', 224, 8, 17, 304885) R. C. If the nations of the world were to consider world government as a means for preserving peace and promoting the welfare of all peoples, would you advocate the abandonment of Indias aspiration for independence ill order to join in the general plan?
('86', 224, 9, 18, 305139) G. If you will carefully go through the much abused Congress resolution of August 1942, you will discover that independence is necessary for India becoming an efficient partner in any scheme for the preservation of lasting peace in the world.

('86', 234, 1, 5, 320731) Shankaracharya says: Sit by the seashore and take one drop of water on a blade of grass.

('86', 234, 1, 7, 321013) March 26, 1945 He who has not in him infinite patience cannot observe non violence.
('86', 234, 1, 8, 321097) March 27, 1945 What is the difference between a snake and a human being?
('86', 234, 1, 9, 321170) Apparently a snake crawls on its belly, while man walks erect on his feet.
('86', 234, 1, 10, 321245) Things are, however, not what they seem to be.
('86', 234, 1, 11, 321292) For what about the man who mentally crawls on his belly?
('86', 234, 1, 12, 321349) March 28, 1945 Every day I see the importance of silence.
('86', 234, 1, 13, 321407) It is good for all, but for him who is deeply absorbed in work, silence is indeed golden.
('86', 234, 1, 14, 321497) March 29, 1945 The hasty are ruffled; the slow and steady have composure. One sees the truth of this every moment.
('86', 234, 1, 15, 321612) March 30, 1945 How dangerous it is to fall out of routine?
('86', 234, 1, 16, 321671) Since coming to Bombay, I have failed to write daily.
('86', 234, 1, 17, 321725) (Written on 3 4 1945.) March 31, 1945 Nothing can work without rules.
('86', 234, 1, 18, 321795) The entire solar system would go to pieces if there were even a momentary breach of the rules governing it.
('86', 234, 1, 19, 321903) (Written on 3 4 1945.) April 1, 1945 This lesson is for all alike, big and small.
('86', 234, 1, 20, 321985) We must learn it and act accordingly, or else die a living death.
('86', 234, 1, 21, 322051) (Written on 3 4 1945.) April 2, 1945 It is sinful to multiply wants unnecessarily.
('86', 234, 1, 22, 322134) (Written on 3 4 1945.)
('86', 235, 0, 1, 322157) 236 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('86', 235, 1, 2, 322199) April 3, 1945 Hartal (general strike) is being observed today for saving the lives of those who have been condemned to the gallows.
('86', 235, 1, 3, 322331) If the days programme is carried out with understanding, we shall have taken a big stride forward on the path of non violence.
('86', 235, 1, 4, 322458) April 4, 1945 Man knows what his duty is, yet does not do what he knows he ought to.
('86', 235, 1, 5, 322543) Why is that so?
('86', 235, 1, 6, 322559) April 5, 1945 We shall be undone if we succumb to the psychological environment around us.
('86', 235, 1, 7, 322650) The situation regarding the Chimur prisoners keeps changing from day to day.
('86', 235, 1, 8, 322727) Let us do our duty and remain detached.
('86', 235, 1, 9, 322767) April 6, 1945 What a high degree of non violence is needed to bear patiently with a person who is bent on misunderstanding even the simplest thing!
('86', 235, 1, 10, 322915) April 7, 1945 I strive hard to preserve my physical body.
('86', 235, 1, 11, 322973) Do I take the same pains to know my soul?
('86', 235, 1, 12, 323015) April 8, 1945 When there is misunderstanding I become angry, I weep, I laugh, I feel pity.
('86', 235, 1, 13, 323106) But instead of this, is it not my duty to keep calm and try to remove the misunderstanding.
('86', 235, 1, 14, 323198) April 9, 1945 What shall we believe?
('86', 235, 1, 15, 323235) Praise of us or censure of us?
('86', 235, 1, 16, 323266) Both may be undeserved.
('86', 235, 1, 17, 323290) Then, shall we be our own judges?
('86', 235, 1, 18, 323324) Here too there is room enough for error.
('86', 235, 1, 19, 323365) God alone knows what we are, but He does not tell us.
('86', 235, 1, 20, 323419) It is, therefore, best neither to seek to know nor believe anything about ourselves.
('86', 235, 1, 21, 323504) We are what we are.
('86', 235, 1, 22, 323524) Nothing is to be gained by knowing or believing what we are.
('86', 235, 1, 23, 323585) Performance of duty is the only thing that really matters.
('86', 235, 1, 24, 323644) April 10, 1945 Blind is not he who has lost his eyes, but he who hides his shortcomings.
('86', 235, 1, 25, 323733) April 11, 1945 Mans serenity of mind can be tested only in the world of men,
('86', 236, 0, 1, 323810) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 237
('86', 236, 1, 2, 323851) not on the solitary heights of the Himalayas.
('86', 236, 1, 3, 323897) April 12, 1945 An ideal is one thing; living up to it is quite another.
('86', 236, 1, 4, 323969) (Written on 15 4 1945.) April 13, 1945 A man without an ideal is like a ship without a rudder.
('86', 236, 1, 5, 324064) (Written on 15 4 1945.) April 14, 1945 I may be said to have an ideal only when I put forth an effort to realize it.
('86', 236, 1, 6, 324181) (Written on 15 4 1945.) April 15, 1945 We may rest content with trying, provided we make the right effort and to the best of our ability.
('86', 236, 1, 7, 324319) The result does not depend on the effort alone.
('86', 236, 1, 8, 324367) There are other factors over which we have no control.
('86', 236, 1, 9, 324422) April 16, 1945 What shall be called the right effort?
('86', 236, 1, 10, 324476) One test is that very often it yields the desired result.
('86', 236, 1, 11, 324534) So the rightness is judged by the result.
('86', 236, 1, 12, 324576) But experience shows that this is not always the case.
('86', 236, 1, 13, 324631) Right effort is that in which there is deep conviction about the correctness of the means employed, so much so that, even in the face of contrary results, the means do not change, nor does the effort vary or slacken.
('86', 236, 1, 14, 324848) April 17, 1945 What shall be called the best of our ability?
('86', 236, 1, 15, 324909) That effort in which we spend all our energy without stint.
('86', 236, 1, 16, 324969) Success generally attends such pure effort.
('86', 236, 1, 17, 325013) April 18, 1945 Man reaches decisions on the strength of insignificant evidence and shapes his course of action accordingly.
('86', 236, 1, 18, 325137) Where such is the case, it is better not to reach a decision as far as possible and to be indifferent as regards the results.
('86', 236, 1, 19, 325263) But should it become a duty to take a decision, it should be taken with the greatest possible care and should be fearlessly implemented.
('86', 236, 1, 20, 325400) April 19, 1945 An important matter loses importance if irrelevant.
('86', 236, 1, 21, 325467) A relevant thing, though small, is of the highest importance.
('86', 237, 0, 1, 325529) 238 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('86', 237, 1, 2, 325571) April 20, 1945 Mans avarice reaches up to the highest heavens and down to the lowest regions of the earth.
('86', 237, 1, 3, 325678) Hence, it should be controlled.
('86', 237, 2, 4, 325710) MAHABALESHWAR, April 21, 1945 Mans joy knows no bounds when he obtains something beyond his hopes.
('86', 237, 2, 5, 325809) April 22, 1945 There is surely something wrong with a person who is supposed to be highly spiritual and yet is always physically ailing.
('86', 237, 2, 6, 325946) April 23, 1945 If we think how enormous is the amount of work we have to do, we shall panic and accomplish nothing.
('86', 237, 2, 7, 326062) Whereas, if we coolly get to grips with it, we shall find that even a mountain of work becomes easier day by day and is ultimately completed.
('86', 237, 2, 8, 326204) April 24, 1945 We do not wish to see our own faults, but take delight in perceiving the faults of others.
('86', 237, 2, 9, 326310) Much unhappiness arises from this habit.

('86', 247, 4, 8, 339518) 430. LETTER TO MUNNALAL G. SHAH
('86', 247, 5, 9, 339550) MAHABALESHWAR, April 26 1945
('86', 247, 6, 10, 339579) MUN NALAL , I got your three letters together.
('86', 247, 6, 11, 339626) I have observed that when you write so many letters at once, you are agitated.
('86', 247, 6, 12, 339705) It is so this time, too.
('86', 247, 6, 13, 339730) Why is that?
('86', 247, 6, 14, 339743) You are agitated when I am in the Ashram and also when I am not.
('86', 247, 6, 15, 339808) Maybe, the nature of your agitation is different in the two cases, but the effect on your health is the same.
('86', 247, 6, 16, 339918) This shows that your unhappiness springs from within, and that its supposed externalcauses are nothing but imagination.
('86', 247, 6, 17, 340038) How can it be that your old co workers themselves harass you?
('86', 247, 6, 18, 340100) The harassment is imagined.
('86', 247, 6, 19, 340128) Differences of opinion do not constitute harassment.
('86', 247, 6, 20, 340181) What is the use of my ordering you?
('86', 247, 6, 21, 340217) After all it is with your co workers that you have to work and you must, therefore, work in harmony with them.
('86', 247, 6, 22, 340328) This is what is meant by public opinion, democracy.
('86', 247, 6, 23, 340380) Work of this nature can be done only by accepting the majority opinion or the decision of the person who has been selected as the leader.
('86', 247, 6, 24, 340518) Why should one feel unhappy about this, or think that ones self respect is being offended?
('86', 247, 6, 25, 340609) This is the only way of serving other peoplenot in the manner we like, but in the manner that they desire.
('86', 247, 6, 26, 340716) Only if you do this cheerfully you will gain wisdom, rise higher and do the utmost possible service.
('86', 247, 6, 27, 340817) My advice, therefore, is that you should remain there and go on working patiently and cheerfully.
('86', 247, 6, 28, 340915) I should, of course, like you to deal with the so called servants as you would with your own brothers and sisters.
('86', 247, 6, 29, 341030) That will bring credit to you, and if you succeed, the results will be excellent.
('86', 247, 6, 30, 341112) Servants have always been with us in their capacity as
('86', 248, 0, 1, 341167) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 249
('86', 248, 1, 2, 341208) servants.
('86', 248, 1, 3, 341218) The only difference is that now we wish to draw them nearer to us and give some time to them.
('86', 248, 1, 4, 341312) If you do not show discretion in this, you will fail.
('86', 248, 1, 5, 341366) But even if you fail, what does it matter?
('86', 248, 1, 6, 341409) Success lies hidden in failure.
('86', 248, 1, 7, 341441) He who fails will one day succeed.
('86', 248, 1, 8, 341476) One who does nothing for fear of failing will achieve nothing.
('86', 248, 1, 9, 341539) If you start re counting from the point where you went wrong, you will get the figure right.
('86', 248, 1, 10, 341632) By losing yourself you will gain yourself.
('86', 248, 1, 11, 341675) One becomes oneself only if one ceases to be oneself.
('86', 248, 1, 12, 341729) Why, then, need you fear losing your individuality?
('86', 248, 1, 13, 341781) Let it be lost.
('86', 248, 1, 14, 341797) I had a letter from Kanchan 1 today, which I am sending for your perusal.
('86', 248, 1, 15, 341871) Let her stay where she is.
('86', 248, 1, 16, 341898) She will get trained there.
('86', 248, 1, 17, 341926) Amtussalaam also mentions her in her letter.
('86', 248, 1, 18, 341971) I am, therefore, sending that too.
('86', 248, 1, 19, 342006) I tear up your letters.
('86', 248, 1, 20, 342030) You should never preserve your letters.
('86', 248, 1, 21, 342070) They contain your sarcasms on the impulse of the moment.
('86', 248, 1, 22, 342127) There is no point in re reading or recalling them.
('86', 248, 1, 23, 342178) All of you have been kept fully informed about ourselves.
('86', 248, 1, 24, 342236) We shall be here up to the end of May, then June in Panchgani and then Sevagram.
('86', 248, 1, 25, 342317) This is my intention.
('86', 248, 1, 26, 342339) Only His will be done.
('86', 248, 1, 27, 342362) Our hosts here are PremliIabehn 2 and Shantikumar 3, and in Panchgani it will beNanji Sheth 4. In addition, Bachchharajbhai 5 is of course at both the places.

('86', 257, 9, 21, 352330) Yarn is a source of strength, as is evident from the very saying: Many threads mean strength. One thread of yarn may snap, but a rope made up of many threads would pull much heavier weight depending on the number of threads...
('86', 257, 9, 22, 352557) 3 Therefore yarn, from a single individual, however much it may be, is of no consequence.
('86', 257, 9, 23, 352647) There will be many who will be ready to give more than seventy six pice...
('86', 257, 9, 24, 352722) It is good that you have decided not to accept more.
('86', 257, 9, 25, 352775) Similarly [even less than that] 4 cannot be accepted.
('86', 257, 9, 26, 352829) Otherwise the account will not be clear.
('86', 257, 9, 27, 352870) Only a little ....

('86', 257, 9, 29, 352963) There are also likely to be millions who

('86', 258, 3, 8, 353603) 447. LETTER TO MANIBEHN PATEL
('86', 258, 4, 9, 353633) MAHABALESHWAR, April 27, 1945
('86', 258, 5, 10, 353663) MAN I, I got your letter.
('86', 258, 5, 11, 353689) Immediately after reading it, I tore it up.
('86', 258, 5, 12, 353733) It had been kept aside by mistake, but it came to me as soon as it was discovered that it was personal.
('86', 258, 5, 13, 353837) But what is there so personal in what you have written?
('86', 258, 5, 14, 353893) I myself opened it just to respect your wishes and to reassure you and will post this in the same way.
('86', 258, 5, 15, 353996) As for fasts, perhaps I must have undertaken more of them than anyone else in the group.
('86', 258, 5, 16, 354085) In South Africa I used to fast on any pretext.
('86', 258, 5, 17, 354132) I must have taken only one meal a day for more than a year.
('86', 258, 5, 18, 354192) But I am of the opinion that moderation in eating is more difficult than fasting.
('86', 258, 5, 19, 354274) Fasts have a place in our life but the death of a relative is certainly not an occasion for them.
('86', 258, 5, 20, 354372) Why shouldnt they be undertaken on the occasion of birth?
('86', 258, 5, 21, 354430) I have done that also but gave that up on further reflection.
('86', 258, 5, 22, 354492) From this you can judge your fasts.
('86', 258, 5, 23, 354528) 1 The human body is the temple of God, and should be taken care of as such.
('86', 258, 5, 24, 354604) It is not that I do not know of your regular habits.
('86', 258, 5, 25, 354657) Motilalji 2
('86', 258, 6, 26, 354669) gave you first rank in that.
('86', 258, 6, 27, 354698) But you should be charitable to co workers.
('86', 258, 6, 28, 354742) You fail in your duty to your neighbours because you are not so.
('86', 258, 6, 29, 354807) Moreover you admit your shortcomings.
('86', 258, 6, 30, 354845) People admit their short comings either because they wish to stick to them or wish to cure themselves of them.
('86', 258, 6, 31, 354956) Dont you wish to get rid of your shortcomings?
('86', 258, 6, 32, 355003) You should infect others with your regularity and at the same time must preserve yours.
('86', 258, 6, 33, 355091) You should act as I do and keep your own

('86', 260, 2, 8, 356991) 449. LETTER TO MOHANLAL BHATT
('86', 260, 3, 9, 357021) MAHABALESHWAR, April 27, 1945
('86', 260, 4, 10, 357051) MOH ANLAL , 2
('86', 260, 5, 11, 357065) Your letter is good.
('86', 260, 5, 12, 357086) It is candid.
('86', 260, 5, 13, 357100) This is my opinion.
('86', 260, 5, 14, 357120) Those who have not taken up Hindustani, or do not know it, learn only half the rashtrabhasha.
('86', 260, 5, 15, 357214) That is why I am partial to Hindustani.
('86', 260, 5, 16, 357254) When we speak of the national language we do include those whose script is Urdu.
('86', 260, 5, 17, 357335) This definition, which I had given at the Sammelan 3, has been accepted.
('86', 260, 5, 18, 357408) Hindi is a language which Hindus and Muslims speak and is written in the Nagari or Urdu script.
('86', 260, 5, 19, 357504) If that is so, you and I have to know both the scripts and be familiar with the vocabulary of both.
('86', 260, 5, 20, 357604) That being the case, you have to revive the Urdu script and always keep in touch with it.
('86', 260, 5, 21, 357694) Besides, in order to remove the feeling of hostility you should join the Hindustani Prachar Sabha.
('86', 260, 5, 22, 357793) If everyone does so, the hostility will be removed.
('86', 260, 5, 23, 357845) I do not yet fully see eye to eye with Tandonji 4. However, we keep exchanging views.
('86', 260, 5, 24, 357931) Indu 5 must have grown up beyond recognition.
('86', 260, 6, 25, 357977) Blessings to you all from BAPU MOHANLAL BHATT 25 NUTAN SOCIETY ELLISBRIDGE, AHMEDABAD From a copy of the Gujarati: Pyarelal Papers.

('86', 263, 0, 1, 361017) 264 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('86', 263, 1, 2, 361059) 454. MESSAGE TO PEOPLE OF CEYLON 1
('86', 263, 2, 3, 361094) MAHABALESHWAR, April 27, 1945
('86', 263, 3, 4, 361124) Gandhiji said that India and Lanka were one, the latter being a pendant of a long chain which was India.
('86', 263, 4, 5, 361229) He said that he had felt that people in Lanka sought to be separated from India, although the culture and problems of both were similar.
('86', 263, 4, 6, 361366) He was glad, however, to learn that there were people in Lanka who realized this unity.
('86', 263, 4, 7, 361454) Such people, he added, needed no message from him.
('86', 263, 4, 8, 361505) They have only to understand the message of the charkha, khadi and the constructive programme, including village uplift and fostering of a national language.
('86', 263, 4, 9, 361663) He referred to his tour of Ceylon 15 years ago 2 and his embarrassment then to notice European and alien habits and customs of the people there, and wished that the Ceylonese had known more about India and the message of the charkha.
('86', 263, 4, 10, 361897) The Bombay Chronicle, 28 4 1945

('86', 278, 2, 3, 380080) MAHABALESHWAR, April 30, 1945
('86', 278, 3, 4, 380110) DEA R AMI YO, Have you worked out the problem of electricity for every home?
('86', 278, 3, 5, 380187) What is the cost?
('86', 278, 3, 6, 380205) My remark quoted by you is a poser for the time being.
('86', 278, 3, 7, 380260) It will cease to be one, if it is a possibility.
('86', 278, 3, 8, 380309) It has not penetrated every home in the villages even of Mysore.

('86', 278, 3, 10, 380555) It is a torture to suffer from fever for years.
('86', 278, 3, 11, 380603) Has the medical profession declared bankruptcy?

('86', 278, 6, 16, 380764) 485. LETTER TO G. V. NARAYANA MURTI
('86', 278, 7, 17, 380800) April 30, 1945 Your information is incomplete.
('86', 278, 7, 18, 380847) How did you get the piles?
('86', 278, 7, 19, 380874) Do you eat hot foods such as chillies and do the piles bleed?
('86', 278, 7, 20, 380936) Meanwhile drink plenty of boiled water, take orange juice and juice of raw vegetable such as carrots, palak and snake gourd.
('86', 278, 7, 21, 381061) You can drink not more than three pounds of milk and take three ounces of fresh coconut well chewed.
('86', 278, 7, 22, 381162) Drink the water of the coconut.
('86', 278, 7, 23, 381194) If the piles bleed, take rest, omit one meal and apply oil to the affected part.

('86', 280, 3, 12, 383486) 488. LETTER TO MUNNALAL G. SHAH
('86', 280, 4, 13, 383518) MAHABALESHWAR, April 30, 1945
('86', 280, 5, 14, 383548) MUN NALAL , Chairman means Chimanlal.
('86', 280, 5, 15, 383586) Inability to come to a decision immediately is no shortcoming, if he is otherwise able to come to a correct decision and express his view in time.
('86', 280, 5, 16, 383733) Chimanlal is the Chairman because he is the most qualified of all.
('86', 280, 5, 17, 383800) But the inmates of the Ashram have a right to appoint another person as Chairman.
('86', 280, 5, 18, 383882) Decide first on who are Ashram inmates.
('86', 280, 5, 19, 383922) If you think it beyond your capacity, the question of majority vote, or for that matter even of one vote, does not arise.
('86', 280, 5, 20, 384044) If all the inmates regard themselves as incapable of running the kitchen, thejoint kitchen should be closed.
('86', 280, 5, 21, 384153) In that case everybody will have to run his own kitchen.
('86', 280, 5, 22, 384210) I do believe, of course, that the Ashram cannot be run in that way.
('86', 280, 5, 23, 384278) It would then be something different.
('86', 280, 5, 24, 384316) I had accepted the suggestion that you should be requested to leave.
('86', 280, 5, 25, 384385) Now I withdraw it fully.
('86', 280, 5, 26, 384410) Remain where you are and prosper.
('86', 280, 6, 27, 384444) Blessings from BAPU

('86', 283, 5, 9, 386609) 494. FOREWORD TO RASHTRABHASHA VISHE VICHAR
('86', 283, 6, 10, 386653) Bhai Jivanji has brought out at the right moment a collection of my writings and speeches on the subject of our national language.
('86', 283, 6, 11, 386784) I have not found it possible to go through all the writings collected here but I have read the first twenty pages.
('86', 283, 6, 12, 386899) I made the first speech 3 on this subject in 1917. And I hold the same views today as those expressed in the speech or thereafter from time to time.
('86', 283, 6, 13, 387048) The only difference is that they are now stronger, clearer and more definite than before.
('86', 283, 6, 14, 387138) Hindi and Urdu have always been inseparable to me.
('86', 283, 6, 15, 387189) I have also quite freely used the word Hindustani.
('86', 283, 6, 16, 387240) I am saying the same thing today that I did in the Hindi Sahitya Sammelan session at Indore in 1918. Hindustani is not Urdu but a happy amalgam of Hindi and Urdu which people in Northern India may easily understand and which may be written either in the Nagari or Urdu script.
('86', 283, 6, 17, 387517) That alone is the perfect national language; all others are imperfect.
('86', 283, 6, 18, 387588) For the present those who desire to learn the national language fully and not partially must learn both the scripts and know both the forms.
('86', 283, 6, 19, 387729) It is a duty demanded of us by our love for the nation.
('86', 283, 6, 20, 387785) Those who learn it will gain, those who do not will lose.
('86', 283, 6, 21, 387843) MAHABALESHWAR, May 1, 1945 [From Gujarati]
('86', 283, 7, 22, 387886) Rashtrabhasha Vishe Vichar.
('86', 283, 7, 23, 387914) Also Pyarelal Papers.
('86', 283, 7, 24, 387936) Courtesy: Pyarelal
('86', 283, 8, 25, 387955) 1 Gandhiji was at Mahabaleshwar from April 21 to May 31, 1945. 2 Dr. Manshankar J. Trivedi 3 At Broach; Speech at Second Gujarat Educational Conference, 20 10 1917.

('86', 291, 1, 2, 396702) 507. LETTER TO KUSUM NAIR
('86', 291, 2, 3, 396728) MAHABALESHWAR, May 2, 1945
('86', 291, 3, 4, 396755) KUSUM, I like your frankness.
('86', 291, 3, 5, 396785) You did well in writing to me.
('86', 291, 3, 6, 396816) I started on the medicine only yesterday.
('86', 291, 3, 7, 396858) It is a new medicine for me and while I am taking it I have to take as much rest as possible.
('86', 291, 3, 8, 396952) It has to be taken for ten days.
('86', 291, 3, 9, 396985) During this time I will not send for you.
('86', 291, 3, 10, 397027) Then there is a meeting 1 of the committee of Kasturba Nidhi.
('86', 291, 3, 11, 397089) After that you can come.
('86', 291, 3, 12, 397114) In the mean time you may send me questions and I will reply to them.
('86', 291, 3, 13, 397183) This time the replies will be only for you.
('86', 291, 3, 14, 397227) I want you to understand me.
('86', 291, 3, 15, 397256) Then you will have your own answer to the day to day questions and you will consult me only if you want my approval for something.
('86', 291, 3, 16, 397387) That is what Mahadev used to do.
('86', 291, 3, 17, 397420) That is what Pyarelal does.
('86', 291, 3, 18, 397448) And, you will be surprised to know, that is, what the late Saunders of Englishman used to do with me.
('86', 291, 3, 19, 397550) Parameshwaran Pillay and Subrahmanyam did the same.
('86', 291, 3, 20, 397602) It will not be too much for you to find time to understand my views fully.
('86', 291, 3, 21, 397677) Accepting them after having understood them is a different question.
('86', 291, 3, 22, 397746) You can differ, and in that case you can bravely oppose me.
('86', 291, 3, 23, 397806) I like genuine opposition.
('86', 291, 3, 24, 397833) About the phone call.
('86', 291, 3, 25, 397855) When you were informed that I was in the bathroom or busy otherwise it was really so.
('86', 291, 3, 26, 397941) There was no thought of deceiving you.
('86', 291, 3, 27, 397980) You must know that from 7.30 to 11.30 I am busy with my routine.
('86', 291, 3, 28, 398045) The work I do during that time is all the work I am able to do.
('86', 291, 3, 29, 398109) After that I have a nap.
('86', 291, 3, 30, 398134) As a result I am ready to see visitors only at 2.30 p.
('86', 291, 3, 31, 398189) This is my normal routine.
('86', 291, 3, 32, 398216) Those who are with me while I am taking my food ask me a few things there and then.
('86', 291, 3, 33, 398300) Bear in mind that the telephone in the house where I live is almost wholly for my use.
('86', 291, 3, 34, 398387) You can ask me further in this connection.
('86', 291, 4, 35, 398430) Blessings from BAPU SHRI KUSUMBEHN NAIR 74 LAKSHMI BUILDING SIR PHEROZESHAH MEHTA ROAD, BOMBAY From a copy of the Hindi: Pyarelal Papers.
