('86', 295, 1, 2, 402121) 515. LETTER TO MANIBEHN PATEL
('86', 295, 2, 3, 402151) MAHABALESHWAR, May 3, 1945
('86', 295, 3, 4, 402178) MANI, I got your letter.
('86', 295, 3, 5, 402203) It is clear.
('86', 295, 3, 6, 402216) As regards your fasts, I suggest that you should undertake them only for reasons of health.
('86', 295, 3, 7, 402308) You will then come to know about yourself, profit from it spiritually too and be emancipated from superstition or insincerity.
('86', 295, 3, 8, 402435) It is quite absurd to think that we should at least fast in memory of Ba or Mahadev if we cannot do anything more.
('86', 295, 3, 9, 402550) They would surely be distressed at this if they could know about it.
('86', 295, 3, 10, 402619) When we lose a dear one, we should do something difficult and at the same time dear to them.
('86', 295, 3, 11, 402712) We might cultivate a sweetness of temper like Mahadevs or faith like Bas.
('86', 295, 3, 12, 402786) I have cited these as two illustrations which readily come to my mind.
('86', 295, 3, 13, 402857) We can think of more.
('86', 295, 3, 14, 402879) If only we realize that the body is the temple of God, or rather the instrument of God realization, all will be well with us.
('86', 295, 3, 15, 403005) Then the fraud which now passes for religion will cease.
('86', 295, 3, 16, 403062) I take all this trouble to explain things to you because you are simple in habits and have resisted many temptations.
('86', 295, 3, 17, 403180) I know that you would be able to achieve much more if you could rise higher in all respects.
('86', 295, 3, 18, 403273) And that is why I wish to draw you here or to the Ashram.
('86', 295, 3, 19, 403331) Father too feels that way, and that makes me all the more eager to attract you.
('86', 295, 3, 20, 403411) If Father was out of prison neither you nor I would desire that even for a single moment you should be anywhere else but by his side.
('86', 295, 3, 21, 403545) If you are near me, you will grow in tolerance, for this is a place where one has to cultivate detachment in spite of having to adjust oneself to different temperaments.
('86', 295, 3, 22, 403715) This means that we should always be ready to learn from others.
('86', 295, 3, 23, 403779) We should observe people, emulate their virtues and bear with their weaknesses for that is the best way of curing them.
('86', 295, 3, 24, 403899) And, therefore, come soon.
('86', 295, 3, 25, 403926) You did well to give me news of Nandubehn, Diwan Master 1 and [Dr.] Kanuga.
('86', 295, 4, 26, 404002) 1 Jiwanlal Diwan
('86', 296, 0, 1, 404019) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 297

('86', 301, 0, 1, 409792) 302 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('86', 301, 1, 2, 409834) 525. TALK WITH D. N. BALAVENKATARAM
('86', 301, 2, 3, 409870) MAHABALESHWAR, May 3, 1945
('86', 301, 3, 4, 409897) Mr. D. N. Balavenkataram, former President of the Salem Taluka Congress Committee, asked Gandhiji whether the Press reports that he would not think of entering the temple of Mahabaleshwar as long as they were not open to the Harijans were correct.
('86', 301, 3, 5, 410145) Mahatma Gandhi remarked: Yes, the Press reports are true.
('86', 301, 3, 6, 410203) As long as the doors of the temples are not open to the Harijans, I shall never enter them.
('86', 301, 4, 7, 410295) Replying to a question whether a visitor should go on a fast unto death to see that the temples were open to the Harijans, Gandhiji said: No.
('86', 301, 4, 8, 410437) That would be an act of violence.
('86', 301, 5, 9, 410471) Asked when a fast was violent and when it could be construed as non violent, Gandhiji replied that it would depend on the circumstances of each case.
('86', 301, 6, 10, 410621) The Bombay Chronicle, 4 5 1945

('86', 302, 1, 2, 411127) 527. STATEMENT TO THE PRESS
('86', 302, 2, 3, 411155) MAHABALESHWAR, May 4, 1945 These are the remarks attributed to Sir Firoz Khan Noon 1 as having been made by him at San Francisco.
('86', 302, 3, 4, 411285) Sir Firoz Khan Noon claimed that while the Japanese were overrunning Burma and heading towards India, the agents of Mahatma Gandhis party severely damaged or destroyed 332 railway stations and 945 post offices.
('86', 302, 3, 5, 411496) He also alleged that Gandhiji himself encouraged disobedience because he was convinced that Britain had been defeated and he did not want to displease the Japanese.
('86', 302, 3, 6, 411661) Gandhiji is in the hands of the reactionary and orthodox Hindus.
('86', 302, 3, 7, 411726) He would be doing a great service to the country if, at this moment, he were to retire in favour of a younger man.
('86', 302, 3, 8, 411841) I feel Nehru would be an excellent successor to Gandhi.
('86', 302, 3, 9, 411897) He has quite a large support among the Muslims and is not so bigoted as Gandhi, who is at a dead end.
('86', 302, 3, 10, 411999) The only solution is for Nehru to come to the forefront.
('86', 302, 3, 11, 412056) But Nehru respects Gandhi so much that he would not come forward. Assuming their authenticity, I beg to offer the following remarks: Time was when I was considered by the British rulers as pro Japanese, but they quietly withdrew the remark.
('86', 302, 3, 12, 412297) There was not the slightest foundation for it.
('86', 302, 3, 13, 412344) It comes somewhat as a surprise that Sir Firoz should make such a statement at this juncture.
('86', 302, 3, 14, 412438) It may interest him to know that even when the British had suffered severe reverses, I told the masses that the British were fighters who were never dismayed by defeats, delighted in bungling and never learned except by making and even repeating mistakes.
('86', 302, 3, 15, 412694) I commend my writings before the August of 1942 to Sir Firoz.
('86', 302, 3, 16, 412756) He will find in them my answer 2 to the Congress Responsibility for the Disturbances, 1942 43. I stood for unadulterated Indianindependence and, therefore, could not afford to be lukewarm about Japanese or any other Powers success against the British.
('86', 302, 3, 17, 413008) My purpose was to end British or any other foreign rule in India as a whole through non violent non co operation and civil resistance.
('86', 302, 4, 18, 413143) 1 Defence Member in the Viceroys Executive Council from October 1943; he was one of the three members of the Indian delegation to the San Francisco Peace Conference; the other two were A. Ramaswami Mudaliar and V. T. Krishnamachari.
('86', 302, 4, 19, 413376) Noon was answering questions in an interview to Indian journalists attending the Conference.
('86', 302, 4, 20, 413469) 2 Vide Letter to Additional Secretary, Home Department, Government of India, 15 7 1943
('86', 303, 0, 1, 413556) 304 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('86', 303, 1, 2, 413598) I had never any party of mine in the Congress.
('86', 303, 1, 3, 413645) I ceased to be its member from December 1934. Whenever my services were needed by the Congress, it had every right to call me in for my special training in non violent resistance.
('86', 303, 1, 4, 413825) Neither the Congress nor I had anything to do with civil or other resistance in and after August 1942. I alone was armed with authority to start it when in my opinion the time for it came.
('86', 303, 1, 5, 414014) But I was arrested before I could take any action or even issue any instructions.
('86', 303, 1, 6, 414096) Therefore neither the Congress nor I could be saddled with any responsibility for the disturbances of 1942. Apart from that fact, the figures quoted by Sir Firoz are utterly unproved, the Government, though often challenged, never having taken the trouble to prove before a competent court of law the charges made by them with surprising lavishness.
('86', 303, 1, 7, 414446) Next, I come to Sir Firozs statement about Pandit Jawaharlal Nehru and me.
('86', 303, 1, 8, 414521) He should know that I have called the Pandit my successor.
('86', 303, 1, 9, 414580) He does not need to come to the front.
('86', 303, 1, 10, 414619) He is in the front.
('86', 303, 1, 11, 414639) The Government of India would not let him work as he would.
('86', 303, 1, 12, 414699) He and I are friends.
('86', 303, 1, 13, 414721) But we are no rivals.
('86', 303, 1, 14, 414743) We are both servants of the people and the platform of service is as big as the world.
('86', 303, 1, 15, 414830) It is never overcrowded.
('86', 303, 1, 16, 414855) On it, there is always room for more, and as on the point of independence we have no differences, we are always brothers in arms.
('86', 303, 1, 17, 414985) He has undoubtedly the advantage of youth over me.
('86', 303, 1, 18, 415036) Let Sir Firoz ask his Government, on pain of resignation, to release Pandit Nehru and his fellow prisoners, and he will see his wish fulfilled.
('86', 303, 1, 19, 415180) I shall give him my hearty co operation in its fulfilment.
('86', 303, 1, 20, 415239) Let him make no capital out of my supposed bigotry or orthodoxy.
('86', 303, 1, 21, 415304) He may not know that I have never been a bigot or known as such since my youth.
('86', 303, 1, 22, 415384) And orthodoxy would not have me for my uncompromising and radical attitude on untouchability and general social reform.
('86', 303, 1, 23, 415504) Sir Firoz is on safer ground when he accuses me of being out of date.
('86', 303, 1, 24, 415574) For no one knows what or who is out of date.
('86', 303, 1, 25, 415619) I confess my ignorance on the point.
('86', 303, 2, 26, 415656) 1 In Mahatma, Vol. 7, p.
('86', 303, 2, 27, 415681) 5, D. G. Tendulkar says: George Bernard shaw stepped in to defend Gandhi: Gandhis politics is half a century out of date.
('86', 303, 2, 28, 415803) His tactics like all tactics are subject to error and readjustment, but his strategy is sound, as it was fifty or five millon years ago. As for Gandhis retiring, he added: Retire from what?
('86', 303, 2, 29, 415993) His position is natural, not official.
('86', 303, 2, 30, 416032) The Mahatma cannot hand over anything.
('86', 303, 2, 31, 416071) Leadership is not a plug of tobacco that can be passed from one man to another. 
('86', 304, 0, 1, 416152) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 305
('86', 304, 1, 2, 416193) I notice too a remark made that the Cripps Mission would have had a greater chance of success, if Mr. Gandhi had not interfered at the last stage.
('86', 304, 1, 3, 416340) It is astonishing how a lie, once it gets a start, persists.
('86', 304, 1, 4, 416401) I left Delhi long before the Mission had commenced its talks with the Working Committee.
('86', 304, 1, 5, 416490) I then ceased to interest myself in the Mission, having more important work on hand.
('86', 304, 2, 6, 416575) The Hindu, 6 5 1945

('86', 310, 0, 1, 423183) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 311
('86', 310, 1, 2, 423224) 539. LETTER TO M. SATYANARAYAN
('86', 310, 2, 3, 423255) May 5, 1945
('86', 310, 3, 4, 423267) SATYANARAYANJI, If you understand individual self reliance, you should understand the self reliance of a society or an institution.
('86', 310, 3, 5, 423399) If an individual believes that he will get his bread if he puts in earnest labour, then the same is true of an institution.
('86', 310, 3, 6, 423523) That is to say, if it renders service, it will get bread without asking, meaning thereby that it will get the money to meet its expenses.
('86', 310, 3, 7, 423661) In fact, it should get the money from its neighbours.
('86', 310, 3, 8, 423715) If it does not get it, then it should realize that no one cares for its services.
('86', 310, 3, 9, 423797) Such a thing can happen while dispelling ignorance in a land of blind faith.
('86', 310, 3, 10, 423874) Then the expenses will be borne by the reformers.
('86', 310, 3, 11, 423924) The same rule will apply here too.
('86', 310, 3, 12, 423959) The reformers in the beginning will starve, a few of them will even die.
('86', 310, 3, 13, 424032) We must have faith that God will sustain them in some way or other.
('86', 310, 3, 14, 424100) If you dont fully understand this, we shall discuss it.
('86', 310, 3, 15, 424156) We wont go further than that.
('86', 310, 3, 16, 424186) I will discuss it only if you want it.
('86', 310, 3, 17, 424225) However, I would love it.

('86', 315, 6, 11, 429840) 549. LETTER TO NARAHARI D. PARIKH
('86', 315, 7, 12, 429874) Not revised May 6, 1945
('86', 315, 8, 13, 429898) NARAHARI, I have gone through your book Kanyane Patro.
('86', 315, 8, 14, 429953) The letters seem to have been written with great care but you have not been bold enough.
('86', 315, 8, 15, 430042) Your views about mixed marriages are not expressed clearly.
('86', 315, 8, 16, 430102) Since I believe that we cannot have too many of such marriages, I do not at all approve of marriages within the same caste.
('86', 315, 8, 17, 430226) I do not find you advocating mixed marriages on an extensive scale even within the same province.
('86', 315, 8, 18, 430324) You accept inter provincial marriages only as exceptions.
('86', 315, 8, 19, 430382) I would encourage them and they ought to be encouraged.
('86', 315, 8, 20, 430438) Reformists, being indifferent to religion, may do that, but their example will have no effect.
('86', 315, 8, 21, 430533) We, however, who keep religion in the forefront should make up our minds how far we are prepared to go.
('86', 315, 8, 22, 430637) If Hindustani becomes the national language and castes and sub castes as we know them disappearas they shouldwe should unhesitatingly accord the highest importance to marriages between Ati Sudras and caste Hindus.
('86', 315, 8, 23, 430851) The question of provincial boundaries will not even arise then.
('86', 315, 8, 24, 430915) Where parents are wise, there should be no difficulty even about marriages between persons of different religions.
('86', 316, 0, 1, 431030) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 317
('86', 316, 1, 2, 431071) Do we not look upon all religions as equal?
('86', 316, 1, 3, 431115) It is with some purpose that we have accorded a place to other faiths in our prayer.
('86', 316, 1, 4, 431200) The offspring may choose either religion.
('86', 316, 1, 5, 431242) The couple of our conception will give the children liberal education in that regard.
('86', 316, 1, 6, 431328) In my view this should be quite easy.
('86', 316, 1, 7, 431366) In letters addressed to a girl, such things should be stated firmly and clearly.
('86', 316, 1, 8, 431447) Mahadevs article is a little out of focus.
('86', 316, 1, 9, 431490) Vanamalas doubt is correct.
('86', 316, 1, 10, 431518) What do our Jain nuns do?
('86', 316, 1, 11, 431544) And what about Swaminarayan nuns?
('86', 316, 1, 12, 431578) It will produce indigestion in the children if we give them so much from English literature.
('86', 316, 1, 13, 431671) Comparisons should be made only between equals.
('86', 316, 1, 14, 431719) Our culture is free from the extremes of Western culture.
('86', 316, 1, 15, 431777) We may know that culture after we have grown up and compare it with ours.
('86', 316, 1, 16, 431851) Growing children should first understand and assimilate their own heritage.
('86', 316, 1, 17, 431927) But I will not make this too long.
('86', 316, 1, 18, 431962) I was forgetting one point.
('86', 316, 1, 19, 431990) You have written with people of our category in view, i.
('86', 316, 1, 20, 432047) e., the upper three castes, and even among them Brahmins and Banias.
('86', 316, 1, 21, 432116) What about Rajputs?
('86', 316, 1, 22, 432136) And Sudras?
('86', 316, 1, 23, 432148) Also Ati Sudras?
('86', 316, 1, 24, 432165) They permit divorce and remarriage.
('86', 316, 1, 25, 432201) There are also communities among whom there is no such thing as marriage ceremony.
('86', 316, 1, 26, 432284) Even then purity is observed.
('86', 316, 1, 27, 432314) This thing must be mentioned.
('86', 316, 1, 28, 432344) Accept from this only what you can assimilate.
('86', 316, 1, 29, 432391) This will give you a glimpse of my latest thinking.
('86', 316, 1, 30, 432443) This is an important letter.
('86', 316, 1, 31, 432472) Make a copy for record in the office or ask Hemantkumar to make one.
('86', 316, 2, 32, 432541) Blessings from BAPU

('86', 318, 0, 1, 433874) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 319
('86', 318, 1, 2, 433915) 552. STATEMENT TO THE PRESS
('86', 318, 2, 3, 433943) MAHABALESHWAR, May 6, 1945
('86', 318, 3, 4, 433970) What do you think of the future plans now being made by the Government to dispose of Indian industries under high sounding phrases, through the nationalist minded Sir Ardeshir Dalal 1 and through the visit of capitalists reported to be presently despatched unofficially to America and England, under the auspices of the Government of India?
('86', 318, 3, 5, 434311) This question has been put to me.
('86', 318, 3, 6, 434345) Nothing said by those outside the Government ring seems to matter.
('86', 318, 3, 7, 434412) They have come to know that the best of us will speak loud and give it the lie by our action.
('86', 318, 3, 8, 434506) Big merchants, capitalists, industrialists and others speak and write against the Government, but in action do its will and even profitthrough itthough the profit may amount to, say, five per cent against the Governments 95. Circumstances alone may be to blame for the condition in which the country has been weltering since the advent of British commerce backed by British guns.
('86', 318, 3, 9, 434886) The bright spot in the situation, however, is that all the big interests proclaim with one voice that India wants nothing less than her own elected national government to shape her own destiny free of all control, British or other.
('86', 318, 3, 10, 435118) This independence will not come for the asking.
('86', 318, 3, 11, 435166) It will come only when the interests, big or small, are prepared to forgo the crumbs that fall to them from partnership with the British in the loot which British rule takes from India.
('86', 318, 3, 12, 435352) Verbal protests will count for nothing so long as the partnership continues unchecked.
('86', 318, 3, 13, 435439) The so called unofficial deputation, which the protestants fear, will go to England and America, dare not proceed, whether for inspection or for entering into a shameful deal, so long as the moving spirits of the Working Committee are being detained without any trial for the sole crime of sincerely striving for Indias independence without shedding a drop of blood save their own.
('86', 318, 3, 14, 435821) The Bombay Chronicle 7 5 1945
('86', 318, 4, 15, 435851) 1 Managing Director, Tata Iron and Steel Company, Bombay; Member, Planning and Development, Viceroys Executive Council
('86', 319, 0, 1, 435970) 320 THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI
('86', 319, 1, 2, 436012) 553. ADVICE TO BRAHMACHARI MAHAVIR 1
('86', 319, 2, 3, 436049) MAHABALESHWAR, [On or before May 7, 1945] 2
('86', 319, 3, 4, 436093) My only advice to you is to go to your own neighbouring villages and serve the villagers there.
('86', 319, 3, 5, 436189) My fifteen point programme is before you.
('86', 319, 3, 6, 436231) Choose any of them and work on it.
('86', 319, 3, 7, 436266) Learn Hindustani, either in the Devanagari or in Urdu script and teach the same to them.
('86', 319, 3, 8, 436355) Learn to clean cotton, spin and weave and teach the same to others.
('86', 319, 3, 9, 436423) No speeches are required but there is the necessity for actual service through work.
('86', 319, 3, 10, 436508) The Hindu, 9 5 1945

('86', 331, 14, 19, 452464) 1 The addressee in his telegram of May 7 had, inter alia, said: I am very much pained .
('86', 331, 14, 20, 452552) that you could have given a public expression of distrust in the bona fides of myself, Tata and Kasturbhai whom you have so well known, and thought that we were going for entering into a deal on behalf of India, shameful or otherwise.
('86', 331, 14, 21, 452787) we know that we have no authority to enter even into a good deal to say nothing of shameful.
('86', 331, 14, 22, 452880) The industrial delegation is going purely as a non official body at its own expense with its own secretariat to England and America with a view to meet people and study the latest methods of production and scientific achievement.
('86', 331, 14, 23, 453110) Your statement is sure to be construed as a strong denunciation of our motives.
('86', 331, 14, 24, 453190) I am leaving Karachi on May 14 and count on your blessings and prayer.
('86', 331, 14, 25, 453261) . 2 Vide Statement to the Press, 6 5 1945. 3 In Mahatma GandhiThe Last Phase, Vol. I, Book One, p.
('86', 331, 14, 26, 453360) 107, Pyarelal explains that Gandhiji defended himself, when objected to by a friend for giving his conditional blessing to the industrialists, saying that is the only way in which ahimsa can act.
('86', 331, 14, 27, 453556) My blessings will haunt like a ghost anyone who contravenes the condition attaching to it. According to Pyarelal, Gandhiji explained, he had put all concerned, including the British Government, on their honour and made it easier for the industrialist friends to put up a fight against any reaction whether within their ranks or without and resist any plan detrimental to Indian interests.
('86', 331, 14, 28, 453945) . 4 In a telegraphic reply dated May 10, the addressee expressed his sense of relief and said he would go with a happy heart.

('86', 333, 1, 2, 455184) 582. TRIBUTE TO RABINDRANATH TAGORE 1
('86', 333, 2, 3, 455222) MAHABALESHWAR, May 8, 1945 Tagore is not only unquestionably the Poet of India or of Asia, but of the whole world.
('86', 333, 2, 4, 455337) It has become the custom among us topay homage to the memory of the great dead not by observing the day of the death anniversary but by observing their birthday.
('86', 333, 2, 5, 455499) The simple reason, perhaps, is that they never die with the dissolution of their bodies.
('86', 333, 2, 6, 455588) Their memory becomes immortal in their works.
('86', 333, 2, 7, 455634) Rama and Krishna were avatars.
('86', 333, 2, 8, 455665) We celebrate their birthdays.
('86', 333, 2, 9, 455695) Similarly, though Gurudev is no longer in flesh among us he will continue to live through his immortal poetry.
('86', 333, 2, 10, 455806) The memory of the Poet will grow richer as years roll by.
('86', 333, 2, 11, 455864) The Hindu, 13 5 1945

('86', 341, 1, 2, 466489) 596. LETTER TO TARACHAND
('86', 341, 2, 3, 466514) MAHABALESHWAR, May 11, 1945
('86', 341, 3, 4, 466542) BHAI TARACHAND, Pandit Sunderlal is here.
('86', 341, 3, 5, 466584) It is good he came.
('86', 341, 3, 6, 466604) I have had talk with him.
('86', 341, 3, 7, 466630) AS a consequence we all feel that there is a danger of being misled if the committee functions at Allahabad.
('86', 341, 3, 8, 466739) Panditji said that those working on the Board 1 will be afraid of going to Wardha and may refuse to go there.
('86', 341, 3, 9, 466849) The implications of this are obnoxious.
('86', 341, 3, 10, 466889) The Sabha was born in Wardha.
('86', 341, 3, 11, 466919) It functioned in Wardha.
('86', 341, 3, 12, 466944) The work on thedictionary should be carried on in Wardha and, if I am to do this work and supervise the dictionary, the office of the Board should be in Wardha.
('86', 341, 3, 13, 467105) There will be nothing to worry about if, for the sake of convenience, some work is done in Allahabad.
('86', 341, 3, 14, 467207) A building was constructed in Wardha for this work.
('86', 341, 3, 15, 467259) Kakasahebs place is in Wardha.
('86', 341, 3, 16, 467290) I am, therefore, of the firm opinion that the headquarters of the Dictionary Board should be in Wardha.
('86', 341, 3, 17, 467394) If Akhtar works for us he should stay in Wardha.
('86', 341, 3, 18, 467443) It will be all right if your own share of work is for the most part sent on to you in Allahabad.
('86', 341, 3, 19, 467540) From this point of view, consideration of expenditure becomes secondary.
('86', 341, 3, 20, 467613) We should now make public the names of the members of the Board we have decided to form, shouldnt we?
('86', 341, 3, 21, 467715) Panditji is writing to the persons concerned.
('86', 341, 3, 22, 467761) We have to have someone take the final decision about the work and then get it approved by the executive committee.
('86', 341, 3, 23, 467877) Isnt that so?
('86', 341, 3, 24, 467891) According to the rules it should be like that.
('86', 341, 3, 25, 467938) Let me know your opinion.
('86', 341, 3, 26, 467964) I am here and in Panchgani till the end of June.
('86', 341, 3, 27, 468013) Panditji is of the opinion that I should be the constitutional head of the Board.
('86', 341, 3, 28, 468095) But I dont think it is necessary.

('86', 345, 8, 14, 473339) On the other hand, the only man who understands and can do your constructive work is myself.

('86', 345, 11, 21, 473672) Horizontal, never vertical.
('86', 345, 11, 22, 473700) But my conception certainly is that we can come to our own if all take up constructive work.
('86', 345, 12, 23, 473793) Parliamentary work will help constructive work.

('86', 359, 1, 2, 493438) 626. LETTER TO IFTIKHARUDDIN 1
('86', 359, 2, 3, 493469) MAHABALESHWAR, [Before May 13, 1945] 2
('86', 359, 3, 4, 493508) DEAR IFTIKHAR 3, Give up the habit of writing and speaking in English, if you want to be free.
('86', 359, 3, 5, 493603) I have read your letter.
('86', 359, 3, 6, 493628) It is my view that no one has the right to speak in the name of the Congress, not even members of the All India Working Committee who are out of jail.
('86', 359, 3, 7, 493779) They can do so only when the whole Committee is out.
('86', 359, 3, 8, 493832) Neither you nor anyone else has the right to work in the name of the Congress.
('86', 359, 3, 9, 493911) This does not mean that you should sit idle and not exercise your influence.
('86', 359, 3, 10, 493988) Nobody can deprive you of your individual position.
('86', 359, 3, 11, 494040) The same applies to members of the Congress Workers Assembly.
('86', 359, 3, 12, 494102) Everyone is his own leader.
('86', 359, 3, 13, 494130) Everyone is free to lead those who follow him.
('86', 359, 3, 14, 494177) This to my mind is the constitutional posi tion.
('86', 359, 3, 15, 494226) Let no one therefore use my name.
('86', 359, 3, 16, 494260) I have not issued any circular.
('86', 359, 3, 17, 494292) 4 What was attributed to me must have been taken from an opinion expressed in a letter I wrote to someone in Ahmedabad.
('86', 359, 3, 18, 494412) All that it meant was that no one can issue orders in the name of the Congress.
('86', 359, 3, 19, 494492) Now as regards your restrictions.
('86', 359, 3, 20, 494526) So long as you do not regard yourself under control of the Government, whatever you wrote (in reply to the restriction order) was correct.
('86', 359, 3, 21, 494665) We must never yield.
('86', 359, 3, 22, 494686) Blessings to you both 5 from BAPU The Hindu, 15 5 1945

Raja gopalachari seeking clarification on an alleged circular by Gandhiji which appeared in The Bombay Chronicle, 2 5 1945. ('86', 364, 6, 23, 502636) All objects of desire are vishayas, as for example, desiring what appeals to the eye, hearing with the ear, smelling with the nose, andother similar objects of sense.

('86', 372, 6, 15, 514219) MANUDI, I can see no difference between your handwriting and Yuktis 1. Instead of myself telling you not to go to Karachi, I told Sushila behn to tell you lest you think I was ordering you.
('86', 372, 6, 16, 514409) If you wishto go either to Karachi or to Porbandar, by all means go.

('86', 372, 6, 18, 514554) If you can do it there, I shall be pleased.
('86', 372, 6, 19, 514598) Because of your negligent habits, I thought that, if you could overcome your fear, you would be able to benefit fully and for long from the mountain air.
('86', 372, 6, 20, 514752) However I am not enamoured of hill stations either.
('86', 372, 6, 21, 514804) Wherever you stay with a free mind, you are bound to benefit.
('86', 372, 6, 22, 514866) You may, therefore, do what your sisters desire.
('86', 372, 6, 23, 514915) I give my consent for it.
('86', 372, 7, 24, 514941) Why should we observe anybodys face?
('86', 372, 7, 25, 514978) We may even make a mistake in judging a person from his face.
('86', 372, 7, 26, 515040) We are not God.
('86', 372, 7, 27, 515056) We might even do him injustice.
('86', 372, 7, 28, 515088) And moreover, when one has made up ones mind not to fear anybody, why need one know the other persons mind?

('86', 387, 4, 6, 532707) 676. FOREWORD TO COW IN INDIA
('86', 387, 5, 7, 532737) One of the first and best pupils of the late lamented Dr. P. C. Ray, Shri Satis Chandra Das Gupta is a fit person to bring under one cover all the available literature on the cow rightly called the Mother of Prosperity.
('86', 387, 5, 8, 532957) By convincing arguments based on copious reading of which he has reproduced the relevant parts in the volume, the author has dispelled the belief held even by learned men that Indias cattle are a burden upon the land and divide its production with the people to the latters detriment.
('86', 387, 5, 9, 533242) He shows the usefulness of the cow as the giver of milk, the producer of draught bullocks, the manurer of our fields and after death the giver of her hide and bone.
('86', 387, 5, 10, 533407) He proves the superiority of cattle over the engine for ploughing the fields of India.
('86', 387, 5, 11, 533494) He establishes the inevitable connection and interdependence between the cattle and other animal life, the earth and man.
('86', 387, 5, 12, 533616) Lastly, he proves the superiority of the cow over the buffalo, not so that the latter should be killed off or starved out but so that the buffalo should not be favoured at the expense of the cow as is done at the present moment.
('86', 387, 5, 13, 533845) I commend the volume to the lover of the cow as also to everyone who would learn that the slaughter of cattle for food is a pure economic waste and know how he can turn the cow into a giver of plenty instead of being the giver of scanty which, owing to criminal negligence, she has become today.
('86', 387, 5, 14, 534141) It will interest the reader to know that the author wrote the whole
('86', 387, 6, 15, 534209) 1 This sentence is in Gujarati.

('86', 388, 1, 2, 534282) volume during his recent imprisonment.

('86', 390, 1, 2, 536751) 681. HOW TO IMPROVE VILLAGE INDUSTRIES
('86', 390, 2, 3, 536790) May 21, 1945 I have distinguished other village industries from khadi and called them planets and the charkha or the spinning wheel the sun.
('86', 390, 2, 4, 536931) As a matter of fact there is no real reason for such a distinction, for khadi is also a village industry.
('86', 390, 2, 5, 537037) But it has acquired a special position, and it is because of this special position which it has acquired that we can now talk about the other village industries.
('86', 390, 2, 6, 537199) Today we are not required to demonstrate the special position acquired by khadi but we are required to discover ways and means of putting it and other village industries on a firm footing.
('86', 390, 2, 7, 537388) One of the ways is to resort to centralized production of necessities through machinery worked by power and requiring the minimum of human labour.
('86', 390, 2, 8, 537535) This results in increasing the number of the rich few and making it a dharma to multiply the peoples wants.
('86', 390, 2, 9, 537643) Even if all such centralized industries were to be State owned, it would make no difference to me.
('86', 390, 2, 10, 537742) For the obligation to increase wants will not only not decrease, but may be strengthened where such industries are owned by the State.
('86', 390, 2, 11, 537877) Only the task of increasing wants will pass from the hands of small capitalists to the bigger capitalists, or the State, whose action will secure the seal of public support.
('86', 390, 2, 12, 538051) This is how things are going in England and America.
('86', 390, 2, 13, 538104) I am purposely leaving out Russia; because their work is still continuing, I shall not at this stage dare to assess the result.
('86', 390, 2, 14, 538232) I hope that Russia will produce something unique.
('86', 390, 2, 15, 538282) But I must confess that I have my doubts whether it will truly succeed.
('86', 390, 2, 16, 538354) I shall consider it a great success if, through it, all the wealth really goes into the hands of the poor, and intellectual and personal freedom is at the same time secured.
('86', 390, 2, 17, 538528) In that case I will have to revise my present concept of ahimsa.
('86', 390, 2, 18, 538593) Now I come to the main point.
('86', 390, 2, 19, 538623) In England and America, machinery rules supreme.
('86', 390, 2, 20, 538672) On the contrary, in India we have village industries, symbolizing the resurgence of human labour.
('86', 390, 2, 21, 538770) In the West, a handful of persons with the aid of mechanical power rule over others.
('86', 390, 2, 22, 538855) In India, on the other hand, the great task of bringing out whatis best in every individual is being attempted by the A. I. S. A., A. I. V. I. A. and other allied institutions.
('86', 390, 2, 23, 539032) From this point of view the growth of Western civilization seems to be an easy thing, but to develop a
('86', 391, 0, 1, 539135) THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI 392
('86', 391, 1, 2, 539177) organize the latent capacities of individuals through village industries appears to be a very difficult task.
('86', 391, 1, 3, 539287) Looking at it from another point of view, it may be said that, for a handful of men to rule over other men with the aid of steam and other power will be harmful in the end, as it is bound to multiply injustice.
('86', 391, 1, 4, 539498) By using the human power available to us by the million, injustice is reduced.
('86', 391, 1, 5, 539577) And there is no room for failure.
('86', 391, 1, 6, 539611) For here, along with human power, we rely on divine Power.
('86', 391, 1, 7, 539670) In the other method, no value is attached to divine Power.
('86', 391, 1, 8, 539729) In short, if in the case of village industries we do not truly obtain Gods help, we are bound to fail.
('86', 391, 1, 9, 539832) The Western method only appears to be successful, but in truth there is nothing but failure in it.
('86', 391, 1, 10, 539931) For it destroys the will to work.
('86', 391, 2, 11, 539965) From a copy of the Hindi: Pyarelal Papers.
('86', 391, 2, 12, 540008) Courtesy: Pyarelal.
('86', 391, 2, 13, 540028) Also Gram Udyog Patrika, June, 1945, Part I, pp.

('86', 399, 3, 9, 550673) She is consumed by fear.
('86', 399, 3, 10, 550698) She herself is the cause of that fear.
('86', 399, 3, 11, 550737) It has become an occupation with her to listen to others, then get upset and jumpy and start crying, and she studies only when she gets some free time from this.
('86', 399, 3, 12, 550899) She is filled with the highest spirit of service, is interested in learning and is of loving nature.
('86', 399, 3, 13, 551000) Like me, she also suffers from amoebiasis and hookworm.
('86', 399, 3, 14, 551056) I keep the infection under control, but she does not.
('86', 399, 3, 15, 551110) Do now whatever suggests itself to you as best.
('86', 399, 3, 16, 551158) She can always come back to me.
('86', 399, 3, 17, 551190) I will never leave her.
('86', 399, 3, 18, 551214) But she is free.

('86', 402, 7, 10, 555301) 704. SPEECH AT HINDUSTAN SCOUT ASSOCIATION TRAINING CAMP 2
('86', 402, 8, 11, 555360) MAHABALESHWAR, May 22, 1945
('86', 402, 9, 12, 555388) Mahatma Gandhi said that the national song which they had sung to welcome him praised Bharatmata and struck a victorious note but the present time was not the one in which one could indulge in joyous celebrations.
('86', 402, 9, 13, 555602) India was now in the same plight as Draupadi was at one time and it was a matter to be seriously considered whether that should be an occasion to celebrate.
('86', 402, 9, 14, 555759) In the song they had sung,there occurred the motto Do or Die.
('86', 402, 9, 15, 555821) That should encourage them to carry on the fight for the liberation of the motherland without rest.
('86', 402, 9, 16, 555921) It was the natural duty of the young to carry on the fight for freedom but at the same time they should not allow the old to take rest.
('86', 402, 9, 17, 556057) The Bombay Chronicle, 23 5 1945
('86', 402, 10, 18, 556089) 1 In the Central Provinces, a number of persons had been sentenced to death in a case of rioting in which some policemen were killed in the villages of Ashti and Chimur during the Quit India movement.
('86', 402, 10, 19, 556290) The King had rejected their mercy petition; vide Statement to the Press, 31 3 1945. But a lacuna in the order was discovered by the defence counsel, and the executions were stayed.
('86', 402, 10, 20, 556471) Later, owing to Gandhijis efforts, on August 16, 1945, the Viceroy commuted the sentences to life imprisonment.
('86', 402, 10, 21, 556583) 2 The camp, organized by Shivaji Troop Boy Scouts of Poona, was addressed by Gandhiji in the evening.

('86', 412, 8, 27, 570051) 2 Bhulabhai Desai, who was preoccupied and also not keeping well, was one of the members of a tribunal suggested by the communists to have the charges against them examined.
('86', 412, 8, 28, 570225) Giving his opinion on August 20, 1945, Desai said that P. C. Joshi had admitted that the war which has ended was a peoples war and that since August 9, 1942, the Communist Party was propagating views contrary to that of the Congress.
('86', 413, 0, 1, 570459) THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI 414
('86', 413, 1, 2, 570501) write to me from the various provinces that communists have no principles save of keeping their party alive and beating their opponents with any stick that came to their hands.
('86', 413, 1, 3, 570678) I am not going to base my opinion on this evidence either.

('86', 418, 11, 18, 579324) 732. LETTER TO PURSHOTTAMDAS TANDON
('86', 418, 12, 19, 579360) MAHABALESHWAR, May 25, 1945
('86', 418, 13, 20, 579388) BHAI TANDONJI,
('86', 418, 14, 21, 579403) I keep receiving letters in Urdu, Hindi and Gujarati all asking me how I can be both in the Hindi Sahitya Sammelan and the Hindustani [Prachar] Sabha at the same time.
('86', 418, 14, 22, 579571) They say that according to the Sammelan Hindi alone can be our national language and the Nagari script alone can be given national status, whereas I concede national status both to the Nagari and Urdu scripts and to a language that is neither too Persianized nor too Sanskritized.
('86', 418, 14, 23, 579852) When I do not accord exclusive national status to the language propagated by the Sammelan and the Nagari script, I ought to get out of the Sammelan.
('86', 418, 14, 24, 580001) It seems to me a valid argument.
('86', 418, 14, 25, 580034) Does it not then become my duty to leave the Sammelan?
('86', 418, 14, 26, 580089) By my doing so people will not be in a dilemma and I shall know where I stand.
('86', 418, 14, 27, 580168) Kindly reply early.
('86', 418, 14, 28, 580188) It being my silence day I myself have
('86', 419, 0, 1, 580226) THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI 420
('86', 419, 1, 2, 580268) written this letter.

('86', 423, 6, 16, 586050) 741. DISCUSSION WITH G. J. M. LONGDEN 1
('86', 423, 7, 17, 586090) MAHABALESHWAR, May 26, 1945 It is understood that Maj.
('86', 423, 7, 18, 586145) Longden, among other things, raised the questions of Dominion Status v.
('86', 423, 7, 19, 586217) Independence, the Hindu Muslim question, responsibility for the August 1942 disturbances and possibility of Congress co operation in the war effort.
('86', 423, 7, 20, 586366) Mahatma Gandhi is said to have replied that the question of Dominion Status v.
('86', 423, 7, 21, 586445) Independence could be decided after the principle of independence for India had been accepted by the British Government.
('86', 423, 7, 22, 586566) On the Hindu Muslim question, Mahatma Gandhi is understood to have said that Hindus who had been converted to Islam could not claim separate nationhood by virtue of a change of religion.
('86', 423, 8, 23, 586753) 1 Conservative Party candidate for the Parliamentary Division of Morpeth (Northumberland) in the British general elections.
('86', 423, 8, 24, 586877) According to the A. P. I. report, Longden was told by Gandhiji that his vow of silence prevented a discussion but that written answers could be given to written questions.
('86', 424, 0, 1, 587049) VOL. 86 : 4 MARCH, 1945 28 MAY, 1945 425
('86', 424, 1, 2, 587090) As regards the August 1942 disturbances, Mahatma Gandhi is said to have declared that the Government themselves have absolved him of charge of treachery and of trying to assist the Japanese.
('86', 424, 1, 3, 587281) Mahatma Gandhi had informed Maj.
('86', 424, 1, 4, 587314) Longden that though he had no objection to the publication of the questions and answers he thought it would be inadvisable to publish them at this stage and Maj.
('86', 424, 1, 5, 587476) Longden agreed.
('86', 424, 2, 6, 587492) The Bombay Chronicle, 28 5 1945
('86', 424, 3, 7, 587524) 742. FOREWORD TO GITAGITMANJARI
('86', 424, 4, 8, 587556) I have discovered no easy way of enjoying the music of songs.
('86', 424, 4, 9, 587618) I cannot, therefore, easily drink in the joy that they are capable of giving.
('86', 424, 4, 10, 587696) It has happened sometimes that when a song was sung in a manner I found sweet, I fully enjoyed it and also understood its meaning.
('86', 424, 4, 11, 587827) Sometimes I myself have been able to hum the tune of a song, and then I have both fully enjoyed the music and understood the meaning.
('86', 424, 4, 12, 587961) Jugatram 1 has requested such a personwith much hesitation to say a few words by way of blessings.
('86', 424, 4, 13, 588060) With much hesitation because he knows the value of my time, as also my limitations.
('86', 424, 4, 14, 588144) If, in spite of that, he has requested my blessings, the reason is that I look upon the Gita as a lexicon of the soul.
('86', 424, 4, 15, 588263) I have not been able to read the Manjari from beginning to end.
('86', 424, 4, 16, 588327) But I have carefully glanced through it.
('86', 424, 4, 17, 588368) I liked the work.
('86', 424, 4, 18, 588386) The authors labour is evident.
('86', 424, 4, 19, 588417) Jugatram has, in his own manner, put into song what he has liked in the different chapters of the Gita.
('86', 424, 4, 20, 588521) The glossary following the Preface in the Manjari, the selected passages from Gitabodh 2 and Anasaktiyog, which are relevant to the context, and the relevant verses from the Gita are likely to prove useful to a serious student of the work.
('86', 424, 4, 21, 588761) Jugatram has not come to the end of his journey.
('86', 424, 4, 22, 588810) He has come as far as Chapter 12. Let us hope that he will be able to complete the journey.
('86', 424, 4, 23, 588902) He has done well also to include, after the 60th manjari, the songs written for Kakasahebs Be Keri 3.
('86', 424, 5, 24, 589004) 1 Jugatram Dave 2 Vide Letters on Gita, 11 11 1930. 3 Literally, Two Mangoes; a Gujarati play written by D. B. Kalelkar; the follow ing item.
('86', 425, 0, 1, 589146) THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI 426
('86', 425, 1, 2, 589188) The student should also know that Jugatram practises the teaching of the Gita as he has understood it, and is one of the few who draw from the fountain of milk unceasingly flowing from it.
('86', 425, 1, 3, 589377) Hence anybody who wishes to enjoy the fragrance of this Manjari should touch it only if he wishes to practise the teaching of the Gita and work in the spirit of non attachment, or derive strength for such work.
('86', 425, 2, 4, 589588) MAHABALESHWAR, May 27, 1945
('86', 425, 3, 5, 589616) M. K. GANDHI
('86', 425, 4, 6, 589629) From a photostat of the Gujarati: S.N. 19336. Also Gitagitmanjari
('86', 425, 5, 7, 589695) 743. LETTER TO JUGATRAM DAVE
('86', 425, 6, 8, 589724) May 27, 1945
('86', 425, 7, 9, 589737) JUG ATRAM , You have given me a good job indeed.
('86', 425, 7, 10, 589786) Here is the Foreword 1, or whatever you care to call it.
('86', 425, 7, 11, 589843) It took more than four hours of my time to write it.
('86', 425, 7, 12, 589896) For me that is too much.
('86', 425, 7, 13, 589921) But I had no choice.
('86', 425, 7, 14, 589942) I like such jobs, but I am no longer fit for them.
('86', 425, 7, 15, 589993) The work which I have planned to do here takes most of my time, or rather all the time that I get.
('86', 425, 7, 16, 590092) My purpose in writing this is not to reproach you for giving me a job like this but, through you, to stop others from doing the same.
('86', 425, 7, 17, 590226) How can I reproach you?
('86', 425, 7, 18, 590250) And then you have written Manjari only to help me in my work.
('86', 425, 7, 19, 590312) Isnt that so?
('86', 425, 7, 20, 590326) This is no mere rhetoric.
('86', 425, 7, 21, 590352) You have called the ninth manjari Samata Yoga and the 40th Samata.
('86', 425, 7, 22, 590419) You will observe that the word samata bears two different meanings in the two places.
('86', 425, 7, 23, 590505) I would call the ninth Samata, dropping Yoga, and the 40th Samatva or Samabhava.
('86', 425, 7, 24, 590586) The reason is plain.
('86', 425, 7, 25, 590607) The discussion of Chapter 12 ends at the 60th manjari.
('86', 425, 7, 26, 590662) I see from the contents that you have included something from Be Keri.
('86', 425, 7, 27, 590733) There should be some mention of it, on p.
('86', 425, 7, 28, 590775) 152 2. Think over it.
('86', 425, 7, 29, 590797) If something can be done about it, do so.
('86', 425, 8, 30, 590839) Blessings from
('86', 425, 10, 31, 590854) From a photostat of the Gujarati: S.N. 19336

('86', 425, 11, 33, 590926) 2 The first song from Be Keri occurs on, this page of Gitagitmanjari.

('86', 426, 1, 2, 591037) 744. LETTER TO SECRETARY, HOME DEPARTMENT, GOVERNMENT OF BOMBAY
('86', 426, 2, 3, 591101) MORARJI CASTLE, MAHABALESHWAR, May 27, 1945 THE SECRETARY TO THE GOVERNMENT OF BOMBAY HOME DEPARTMENT BOMBAY
('86', 426, 3, 4, 591210) DEAR SIR, I refer you to my letter 1 of 6th May, 1944, written from the Detention Camp.
('86', 426, 3, 5, 591298) Up till recently there has been no hitch about friends and relatives going to the samadhis of the two departed ones, my wife and Shri Mahadev Desai.
('86', 426, 3, 6, 591447) But a hitch occurred recently.
('86', 426, 3, 7, 591478) Tactful handling made devotion fairly possible during fixed hours.
('86', 426, 3, 8, 591545) Now comes the rumour that H. H. the Aga Khans Palace is about to be occupied by the Military and in that event, devotion may not be permitted at all.
('86', 426, 3, 9, 591695) I can only hope that the fear is wholly unjustified.
('86', 426, 3, 10, 591748) In my letter of 6th May, 1944, to the Government I reduced my contention to writing to the effect that
('86', 426, 4, 11, 591851) by reason of the cremation of the corpses of Shri Mahadev Desai and then my wife, the place of cremation which has been fenced off becomes consecrated ground.
('86', 426, 4, 12, 592010) The party has daily visited the ground twice and offered floral tributes to the departed spirits and said prayers.
('86', 426, 4, 13, 592125) I trust that the plot will be acquired by the Government with the right of way to it through H. H. the Aga Khans grounds so as to enable those relatives and friends who wish to visit the cremation ground whenever they like.
('86', 426, 4, 14, 592349) To this the following reply was received:
('86', 426, 5, 15, 592391) I am to inform you that it is legally impossible for Government to acquire the site compulsorily under the Land Acquisition Act.
('86', 426, 5, 16, 592520) Government considers that the matter is one for private negotiations between you and His Highness the Aga Khan.
('86', 426, 5, 17, 592632) I am to add, however, that your request has been communicated to His Highness the Aga Khan and is now understood to be under his consideration.
('86', 426, 5, 18, 592776) Government understands that he has no objection, in the mean while, to the relatives of Mrs. Gandhi and Mr. Mahadev Desai and any other persons suggested by you going through the Palace
('86', 426, 6, 19, 592962) 1 Vide Letter to Secretary, Home Department, Government of Bombay, 6 5 1944.
('86', 427, 0, 1, 593039) THE COLLECTED WORKS OF MAHATMA GANDHI 428
('86', 427, 1, 2, 593081) grounds to the place of cremation on the understanding that this is by his leave and licence.
('86', 427, 1, 3, 593175) I do hope that, no matter who occupies or owns the palace, the consecrated ground on which the two samadhis stand will be protected and reserved for devotion by the friends and relatives of the families.
('86', 427, 2, 4, 593379) I am, etc., M. K. GANDHI
('86', 427, 3, 5, 593404) From a photostat: G.N. 3940

('86', 429, 1, 2, 595705) 748. LETTER TO BHARATAN KUMARAPPA
('86', 429, 2, 3, 595739) May 28, 1945
('86', 429, 3, 4, 595752) MY DEAR BHARATAN, Your letter and the book.
('86', 429, 3, 5, 595796) 1 Appasamy came, left the book and went away.
('86', 429, 3, 6, 595842) I have not met him.
('86', 429, 3, 7, 595862) I wonder if he will seek me out and meet me though I am silent the whole day till evening prayer!
('86', 429, 3, 8, 595960) You need not apologize for sending me the book.
('86', 429, 3, 9, 596008) I must read it.
('86', 429, 3, 10, 596024) I glanced at it, as it came into my hands.
('86', 429, 3, 11, 596067) How does it differ from your description of socialism which you say centres round society and its needs and villagism which you say centres round the village and its wants?
('86', 429, 3, 12, 596240) Do you mark any difference?
('86', 429, 3, 13, 596268) Is not village and its welfare the same as society and its needs?
('86', 429, 3, 14, 596334) Is not the difference this: socialism includes violence as a measure to achieve it, villagism excludes it?
('86', 429, 3, 15, 596441) My English is not perfect.
('86', 429, 3, 16, 596468) It may be relatively better than Hindustani.
('86', 429, 3, 17, 596513) I must try to make it equal to my English, if it is not.
('86', 429, 3, 18, 596570) I reach the masses only through Hindustani however imperfect it may be, never through English, however perfect it may be.
('86', 429, 3, 19, 596692) If you admit this, the Patrika would be only in Hindustani and the provinces will render it in the provincial languages, the people thereof will understand.
('86', 429, 3, 20, 596849) You may have an English translation of necessary extracts for the foreign reader.
('86', 429, 3, 21, 596931) This can happen only when both of you see the point and resolve to write in Hindustani however imperfect it may be.
('86', 429, 3, 22, 597047) I migrate to Panchgani on 31st May.

('86', 438, 3, 4, 606345) KRI SHNAC HANDR A, Do not worry about Balkobas discharge.

('86', 438, 3, 13, 606685) Shriman has taken his argument to the extreme.
('86', 438, 3, 14, 606732) It is impossible today.
('86', 438, 3, 15, 606756) Ramdas does not know the whole of India directly or indirectly.
('86', 438, 3, 16, 606820) It is not his fault.
('86', 438, 3, 17, 606841) One must be acquainted with the situation in India in order to make a scientific study.
('86', 438, 3, 18, 606929) The situation about which he is talking is due to the invasion from the West.
('86', 438, 3, 19, 607007) There can only be violence at the root of Ramdass statement.
('86', 438, 3, 20, 607068) If non violence has to prevail, many things will have to be carried on without steam power, etc.

('86', 440, 1, 2, 608320) APPENDICES
('86', 440, 2, 3, 608331) APPENDIX I
('86', 440, 3, 4, 608342) PYARELALS STATEMENT1
('86', 440, 4, 5, 608363) Gandhiji, having seen it, says that he never sent any such or other circular to Congress workers or committees in any or all the Provinces.
('86', 440, 4, 6, 608503) The statement that has appeared in the Press to that effect is, therefore, wrong.
('86', 440, 4, 7, 608585) He holds the view, and has shared it with correspondents, that as long as the Congress President and his colleagues are in prison, Congressmen must act on their own initiative and judgment and no individual or group or assembly, whatever name they give to themselves, will have the authority to act in the name or on behalf of the Congress organization.
('86', 440, 4, 8, 608939) They are entitled to and bound to act as they deem it best in the interests of the cause for which the Congress stands, but they do so on their own authority and responsibility and cannot use the name of the Congress to enforce their decision.
('86', 440, 4, 9, 609183) Gandhiji adds that such is his individual opinion.
('86', 440, 5, 10, 609234) The Bombay Chronicle, 11 5 1945
('86', 440, 6, 11, 609266) 1 Vide p.
